Welcome to Dune Docs

[Get Started](https://docs.dune.com/home)

On this page

*   [Go through our YouTube Tutorials](https://docs.dune.com/home#go-through-our-youtube-tutorials)
    
*   [Start building](https://docs.dune.com/home#start-building)
    
*   [Learn more](https://docs.dune.com/home#learn-more)
    
*   [Why Dune?](https://docs.dune.com/home#why-dune%3F)
    

Blockchains are open and transparent, but each chain is unique—making it difficult to understand, ingest, and aggregate data. Dune gives you the tools to analyze cross-chain data for different tokens, wallets, and protocols. You can also easily share your work with the community, export and integrate data into your own applications, and more.

### 

[​](https://docs.dune.com/home#go-through-our-youtube-tutorials)

Go through our YouTube Tutorials

We’ve created tutorials covering all product surfaces of Dune, how to navigate and understand all tables, and how to level up as a crypto data analyst. [Check out the full playlist.](https://www.youtube.com/playlist?list=PLK3b5d4iK10ext4v-GBySekaA8-GP8quD)

### 

[​](https://docs.dune.com/home#start-building)

Start building

Ready to start building? Once you have an [account](https://dune.com/auth/register)
 and you have reviewed the [Quickstart](https://docs.dune.com/quickstart)
, check out these essentials to start using Dune.

[Web App\
-------\
\
Learn about the Dune Web App, your portal to creating, viewing, and interacting with blockchain analytics dashboards.](https://docs.dune.com/web-app)
[Data Catalog\
------------\
\
Explore our comprehensive Data Catalog to find and utilize the exact datasets you need for your queries and analytics.](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog)
[API\
---\
\
Integrate Dune directly into your workflow with our API, allowing for automated data extraction and analysis.](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference)
[Query Engine\
------------\
\
Discover the power of the Dune Query Engine to execute advanced SQL queries and analyze blockchain data.](https://docs.dune.com/query-engine)
[Alerts\
------\
\
Set up alerts to be notified when specific conditions are met in the data.](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/alerts)

**Quickstart** To get started with Dune in 5 minutes, see the [Quickstart](https://docs.dune.com/quickstart)
.

### 

[​](https://docs.dune.com/home#learn-more)

Learn more

If you are new to blockchain or SQL —or want to go deeper on Dune concepts and best practices— check out the following resources:

*   [Dune Official Getting Started Video Series](https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=S-cctFmR828&list=PLK3b5d4iK10ext4v-GBySekaA8-GP8quD&index=1)
     to learn how data flows and how to navigate the Dune app to get the most out of it
*   Join our community in [Discord](https://discord.gg/FjwGvbgDFS)
     to get support through the `#🐥︱beginners` and `#🙋︱query-questions` channels

You can also level up by following the [crypto data analyst roadmap](https://roadmap.sh/r?id=65fee5b66deb533d6e19fb88)
:

### 

[​](https://docs.dune.com/home#why-dune%3F)

Why Dune?

Dune—along with our massive community of users and experts—provides powerful tools and analysis of all onchain data. You can find a [dashboard](https://dune.com/browse/dashboards?q=dex&order=favorites&time_range=all)
 for pretty much anything web3-related, including for EVMs like Ethereum, Polygon, Goerli, and Optimism—and non-EVM chains like Solana and Bitcoin. Examples of real dashboards:

*   [NFT marketplaces](https://dune.com/hildobby/ethereum-nfts)
    
*   [DEX metrics](https://dune.com/hagaetc/dex-metrics)
    
*   [Project metrics](https://dune.com/whale_hunter/unibot-revenue)
    
*   [DAO Accounting (Maker)](https://dune.com/steakhouse/makerdao)
    
*   [Base Chain Metrics](https://dune.com/optimismfnd/Optimism)

      "state": "QUERY_STATE_COMPLETED",
      "submitted_at": "2024-12-20T11:04:18.724658237Z"
    }

*   Query can be found [here](https://dune.com/queries/3568055)
    
*   Chains included are: `arbitrum`, `base`, `bnb`, `celo`, `ethereum`, `fantom`, `gnosis`, `optimism`, `polygon`, `scroll`, `zk_sync`, `solana`
*   Scheduled to update every 30 minutes
*   You can apply [filters](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/executions/filtering)
     like WHERE, IN, AND/OR upon results
*   Each row is uniquely identified by the `chain`, `token_a_address`, and `token_b_address` columns combination.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/dex/endpoint/dex_pair#use-cases)

Use Cases
=====================================================================================

*   Enable DEX aggregators to identify all pools for swapping specific token pairs or addresses, using filters such as `filter='USDC-WETH'` or `filters=token_a_address = '0xa0b86991c6218b36c1d19d4a2e9eb0ce3606eb48' or token_b_address = '0xa0b86991c6218b36c1d19d4a2e9eb0ce3606eb48'`.
*   Identify the token pair with the highest USD liquidity on a given chain by sorting results with `sort_by=usd_liquidity desc`.
*   Provide aggregated DEX pair statistics, including volume and liquidity, to algorithmic trading bots and risk management systems.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/dex/endpoint/dex_pair#column-descriptions)

Column Descriptions
=========================================================================================================

| Column | Description | Type |
| --- | --- | --- |
| chain | The blockchain where the token pair is traded | string |
| token\_pair | The identifier of the token pair, e.g., ‘USDC-WETH’ | string |
| projects | List of DEX projects offering the token pair | array(string) |
| pool\_ids | Contract addresses of pools containing the token pair | array(string) |
| token\_a\_address | Contract address of the first token in the pair | string |
| token\_b\_address | Contract address of the second token in the pair | string |
| one\_day\_volume | 24-hour USD trading volume for the token pair across all pools on all DEXes | double |
| seven\_day\_volume | 7-day USD trading volume for the token pair across all pools on all DEXes | double |
| thirty\_day\_volume | 30-day USD trading volume for the token pair across all pools on all DEXes | double |
| all\_time\_volume | Total USD trading volume for the token pair since inception across all pools on all DEXes | double |
| usd\_liquidity | Current USD liquidity available in all pools for the token pair on all DEXes | double |
| seven\_day\_volume\_liquidity\_ratio | 7-day trading volume to liquidity ratio for the token pair across all pools on all DEXes | double |

#### Headers

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/dex/endpoint/dex_pair#parameter-x-dune-api-key)

X-Dune-Api-Key

string

required

API Key for the service

#### Path Parameters

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/dex/endpoint/dex_pair#parameter-chain)

chain

string

required

The blockchain where the token pair is traded

#### Query Parameters

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/dex/endpoint/dex_pair#parameter-api-key)

api\_key

string

API Key, alternative to using the HTTP header X-Dune-Api-Key

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/dex/endpoint/dex_pair#parameter-allow-partial-results)

allow\_partial\_results

boolean

This enables returning a query result that was too large and only a partial result is available. By default allow\_partial\_results is set to false and a failed state is returned.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/dex/endpoint/dex_pair#parameter-columns)

columns

string

Specifies a comma-separated list of column names to return. If omitted, all columns are included. Tip: use this to limit the result to specific columns, reducing datapoints cost of the call.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/dex/endpoint/dex_pair#parameter-filters)

filters

string

Expression to filter out rows from the results to return. This expression is similar to a SQL WHERE clause. More details about it in the Filtering section of the doc. This parameter is incompatible with sample\_count.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/dex/endpoint/dex_pair#parameter-ignore-max-datapoints-per-request)

ignore\_max\_datapoints\_per\_request

boolean

There is a default 250,000 datapoints limit to make sure you don't accidentally spend all your credits in one call. To ignore the max limit, you can add ignore\_max\_datapoints\_per\_request=true

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/dex/endpoint/dex_pair#parameter-limit)

limit

integer

Limit number of rows to return. This together with 'offset' allows easy pagination through results in an incremental and efficient way. This parameter is incompatible with sampling (sample\_count).

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/dex/endpoint/dex_pair#parameter-offset)

offset

integer

Offset row number to start (inclusive, first row means offset=0) returning results from. This together with 'limit' allows easy pagination through results in an incremental and efficient way. This parameter is incompatible with sampling (sample\_count).

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/dex/endpoint/dex_pair#parameter-query-id)

queryID

integer

required

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/dex/endpoint/dex_pair#parameter-sample-count)

sample\_count

integer

Number of rows to return from the result by sampling the data. This is useful when you want to get a uniform sample instead of the entire result. If the result has less than the sample count, the entire result is returned. Note that this will return a randomized sample, so not every call will return the same result. This parameter is incompatible with `offset`, `limit`, and `filters` parameters.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/dex/endpoint/dex_pair#parameter-sort-by)

sort\_by

string

Expression to define the order in which the results should be returned. This expression is similar to a SQL ORDER BY clause. More details about it in the Sorting section of the doc.

#### Response

200

application/json

OK

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/dex/endpoint/dex_pair#response-cancelled-at)

cancelled\_at

string

Timestamp of when the query execution was cancelled, if applicable.

Example:

`"2024-12-20T11:04:18.724658237Z"`

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/dex/endpoint/dex_pair#response-error)

error

object

In case the execution had an error, this object will contain the error details

Show child attributes

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/dex/endpoint/dex_pair#response-execution-ended-at)

execution\_ended\_at

string

Timestamp of when the query execution ended.

Example:

`"2024-12-20T11:04:18.724658237Z"`

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/dex/endpoint/dex_pair#response-execution-id)

execution\_id

string

Unique identifier for the execution of the query.

Example:

`"01HKZJ2683PHF9Q9PHHQ8FW4Q1"`

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/dex/endpoint/dex_pair#response-execution-started-at)

execution\_started\_at

string

Timestamp of when the query execution started.

Example:

`"2024-12-20T11:04:18.724658237Z"`

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/dex/endpoint/dex_pair#response-expires-at)

expires\_at

string

Timestamp of when the query result expires.

Example:

`"2024-12-20T11:04:18.724658237Z"`

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/dex/endpoint/dex_pair#response-is-execution-finished)

is\_execution\_finished

boolean

Whether the state of the query execution is terminal. This can be used for polling purposes.

Example:

`true`

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/dex/endpoint/dex_pair#response-next-offset)

next\_offset

integer

Offset that can be used to retrieve the next page of results.

Example:

`100`

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/dex/endpoint/dex_pair#response-next-uri)

next\_uri

string

URI that can be used to fetch the next page of results.

Example:

`"https://api.dune.com/api/v1/execution/01HKZJ2683PHF9Q9PHHQ8FW4Q1/results?offset=100&limit=100"`

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/dex/endpoint/dex_pair#response-query-id)

query\_id

integer

Unique identifier of the query.

Example:

`1234`

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/dex/endpoint/dex_pair#response-result)

result

object

The object containing the results and metadata of the query execution

Show child attributes

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/dex/endpoint/dex_pair#response-state)

state

string

The state of the query execution.

Example:

`"QUERY_STATE_COMPLETED"`

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/dex/endpoint/dex_pair#response-submitted-at)

submitted\_at

string

Timestamp of when the query was submitted.

Example:

`"2024-12-20T11:04:18.724658237Z"`

*   Query powering this endpoint can be found [here](https://dune.com/queries/3685760)
    
*   Scheduled to update every 15 minutes
*   Apply [filters](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/executions/filtering)
     like WHERE, IN, AND/OR upon results
*   Use a combination of `sort_by` and `limit` to grab a subset of results, see [pagination](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/executions/pagination)
     and [sorting](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/executions/sorting)
     for more info

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/eigenlayer/endpoint/operator_metadata#column-descriptions)

Column Descriptions
=========================================================================================================================

| Column | Description | Type |
| --- | --- | --- |
| operator\_name | Name of the operator | string |
| operator\_contract\_address | Ethereum contract address of the operator | string |
| website | Website URL of the operator | string |
| twitter | Twitter link of the operator | string |
| logo | URL to the logo image of the operator | string |
| description | Brief description of the operator | string |

#### Headers

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/eigenlayer/endpoint/operator_metadata#parameter-x-dune-api-key)

X-Dune-Api-Key

string

required

API Key for the service

#### Query Parameters

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/eigenlayer/endpoint/operator_metadata#parameter-api-key)

api\_key

string

API Key, alternative to using the HTTP header X-Dune-Api-Key

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/eigenlayer/endpoint/operator_metadata#parameter-allow-partial-results)

allow\_partial\_results

boolean

This enables returning a query result that was too large and only a partial result is available. By default allow\_partial\_results is set to false and a failed state is returned.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/eigenlayer/endpoint/operator_metadata#parameter-columns)

columns

string

Specifies a comma-separated list of column names to return. If omitted, all columns are included. Tip: use this to limit the result to specific columns, reducing datapoints cost of the call.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/eigenlayer/endpoint/operator_metadata#parameter-filters)

filters

string

Expression to filter out rows from the results to return. This expression is similar to a SQL WHERE clause. More details about it in the Filtering section of the doc. This parameter is incompatible with sample\_count.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/eigenlayer/endpoint/operator_metadata#parameter-ignore-max-datapoints-per-request)

ignore\_max\_datapoints\_per\_request

boolean

There is a default 250,000 datapoints limit to make sure you don't accidentally spend all your credits in one call. To ignore the max limit, you can add ignore\_max\_datapoints\_per\_request=true

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/eigenlayer/endpoint/operator_metadata#parameter-limit)

limit

integer

Limit number of rows to return. This together with 'offset' allows easy pagination through results in an incremental and efficient way. This parameter is incompatible with sampling (sample\_count).

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/eigenlayer/endpoint/operator_metadata#parameter-offset)

offset

integer

Offset row number to start (inclusive, first row means offset=0) returning results from. This together with 'limit' allows easy pagination through results in an incremental and efficient way. This parameter is incompatible with sampling (sample\_count).

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/eigenlayer/endpoint/operator_metadata#parameter-query-id)

queryID

integer

required

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/eigenlayer/endpoint/operator_metadata#parameter-sample-count)

sample\_count

integer

Number of rows to return from the result by sampling the data. This is useful when you want to get a uniform sample instead of the entire result. If the result has less than the sample count, the entire result is returned. Note that this will return a randomized sample, so not every call will return the same result. This parameter is incompatible with `offset`, `limit`, and `filters` parameters.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/eigenlayer/endpoint/operator_metadata#parameter-sort-by)

sort\_by

string

Expression to define the order in which the results should be returned. This expression is similar to a SQL ORDER BY clause. More details about it in the Sorting section of the doc.

# Dune EigenLayer Endpoints - Dune Docs

[Skip to main content](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/eigenlayer/introduction#content-area)

[Dune Docs home page![light logo](https://mintcdn.com/dune/uyJ-jHeSRFvNrzyu/logo/dune-logo-light.png?fit=max&auto=format&n=uyJ-jHeSRFvNrzyu&q=85&s=fbdf0e7e6fabc31e49afcdb53cb5e774)![dark logo](https://mintcdn.com/dune/uyJ-jHeSRFvNrzyu/logo/dune-logo-dark.png?fit=max&auto=format&n=uyJ-jHeSRFvNrzyu&q=85&s=767370d661596e21a7b3a4525d50d77e)](https://dune.com/)

Search...

⌘K

Search...

Navigation

EigenLayer

Dune EigenLayer Endpoints

[Get Started](https://docs.dune.com/home)
[Analytics Studio](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/overview)
[Query Engine](https://docs.dune.com/query-engine/overview)
[Data Catalog](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/overview)
[Analytics API](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/overview/introduction)
[Datashare](https://docs.dune.com/datashare/datashare)
[Catalyst](https://docs.dune.com/catalyst/overview)

Leverage Dune’s API for direct access to [EigenLayer](https://www.eigenlayer.xyz/)
 data, streamlining your dApp and infrastructure development. No SQL needed—our Domain-specific API is designed for easy integration and flexible application use.

*   **JSON Format**: All endpoints deliver JSON-formatted data for straightforward integration.
*   **Instant Access**: Begin immediately by [creating a free account](https://dune.com/auth/register)
     and [obtain an API key](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/overview/authentication)
    .
*   **Expansive Data Ecosystem**: Enhance your projects by connecting with an extensive range of on-chain and off-chain data, from [Farcaster](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/farcaster/introduction)
     to [DEX](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/dex/endpoint/dex_pair.mdx)
     and more. Build alongside our vibrant community.

[AVS Metadata\
------------\
\
Get AVS metadata, including name, address, and more.](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/eigenlayer/endpoint/avs_metadata)
[Operator Metadata\
-----------------\
\
Get operator metadata, including name, address, and more.](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/eigenlayer/endpoint/operator_metadata)
[AVS Metrics\
-----------\
\
Get AVS metrics, including TVL, number of operators and number of stakers.](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/eigenlayer/endpoint/avs_metrics)
[Operator Metrics\
----------------\
\
Get operator metrics, including TVL, number of stakers, and more.](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/eigenlayer/endpoint/operator_metrics)
[Operator <> AVS Mapping\
-----------------------\
\
Get a mapping of which operator is registered to which AVS and when it was registered.](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/eigenlayer/endpoint/operator_to_avs_mapping)

  

To custom-build an API endpoint with SQL query, watch [this short video](https://youtu.be/o29ig849qMY)
 and [get started here](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/quickstart/results-eg)
!

      --url https://api.dune.com/api/v1/trends/evm/contracts/{chain} \
      --header 'X-Dune-Api-Key: <x-dune-api-key>'

Ask AI

    {
      "cancelled_at": "2024-12-20T11:04:18.724658237Z",
      "error": {
        "message": "Error: Line 1:1: mismatched input 'selecdt'",
        "metadata": {
          "column": 73,
          "line": 10
        },
        "type": "syntax_error"
      },
      "execution_ended_at": "2024-12-20T11:04:18.724658237Z",
      "execution_id": "01HKZJ2683PHF9Q9PHHQ8FW4Q1",
      "execution_started_at": "2024-12-20T11:04:18.724658237Z",
      "expires_at": "2024-12-20T11:04:18.724658237Z",
      "is_execution_finished": true,
      "next_offset": 100,
      "next_uri": "https://api.dune.com/api/v1/execution/01HKZJ2683PHF9Q9PHHQ8FW4Q1/results?offset=100&limit=100",

          "column_names": [\
            "Rank",\
            "Project",\

            "double",\

          "pending_time_millis": 1000,
          "result_set_bytes": 1000,
          "row_count": 10,
          "total_result_set_bytes": 10000,
          "total_row_count": 1000
        },
        "rows": [\
          {}\
        ],
        "update_type": "<string>"
      },
      "state": "QUERY_STATE_COMPLETED",
      "submitted_at": "2024-12-20T11:04:18.724658237Z"
    }

*   Query can be found [here](https://dune.com/queries/3575084)
    
*   Scheduled to update once a day (12am UTC)
*   You can apply [filters](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/executions/filtering)
     like WHERE, IN, AND/OR upon results

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/evm/endpoint/contracts#use-cases)

Use Cases
======================================================================================

*   Feed into a CRM of developers and projects based on contract popularity
*   Build an explorer page of top trending contracts with basic metadata support.
*   Track trending contracts by value and type (user facing, contract facing, token, router, safes, etc.)

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/evm/endpoint/contracts#column-descriptions)

Column Descriptions
==========================================================================================================

| Column Name | Description | Type |
| --- | --- | --- |
| contract\_address | Contract address of the contract | string |
| blockchain | Blockchain of the contract | string |
| deployer | Deployer address of the contract | string |
| contract\_project | Project of the contract | string |
| contract\_name | Name of the contract | string |
| created\_time | Time when the contract was created | string |
| deployed\_days\_ago | Number of days since deployment | integer |
| token\_standard | Standard of the token (ERC20, ERC721, ERC1155) if applicable | string |
| usd\_value\_received | Value received in USD in ETH and ERC20 tokens in last 30 days | integer |
| transaction\_calls | Number of transaction calls (top level transactions) in last 30 days | integer |
| unique\_callers | Number of unique callers (tx from) in last 30 days | integer |
| contract\_calls | Number of calls from other contracts in last 30 days | integer |
| unique\_contract\_callers | Number of unique contracts calling this contract in traces in last 30 days | integer |

#### Headers

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/evm/endpoint/contracts#parameter-x-dune-api-key)

X-Dune-Api-Key

string

required

API Key for the service

#### Path Parameters

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/evm/endpoint/contracts#parameter-chain)

chain

string

required

The blockchain where the token pair is traded

#### Query Parameters

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/evm/endpoint/contracts#parameter-api-key)

api\_key

string

API Key, alternative to using the HTTP header X-Dune-Api-Key

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/evm/endpoint/contracts#parameter-allow-partial-results)

allow\_partial\_results

boolean

This enables returning a query result that was too large and only a partial result is available. By default allow\_partial\_results is set to false and a failed state is returned.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/evm/endpoint/contracts#parameter-columns)

columns

string

Specifies a comma-separated list of column names to return. If omitted, all columns are included. Tip: use this to limit the result to specific columns, reducing datapoints cost of the call.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/evm/endpoint/contracts#parameter-filters)

filters

string

Expression to filter out rows from the results to return. This expression is similar to a SQL WHERE clause. More details about it in the Filtering section of the doc. This parameter is incompatible with sample\_count.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/evm/endpoint/contracts#parameter-ignore-max-datapoints-per-request)

ignore\_max\_datapoints\_per\_request

boolean

There is a default 250,000 datapoints limit to make sure you don't accidentally spend all your credits in one call. To ignore the max limit, you can add ignore\_max\_datapoints\_per\_request=true

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/evm/endpoint/contracts#parameter-limit)

limit

integer

Limit number of rows to return. This together with 'offset' allows easy pagination through results in an incremental and efficient way. This parameter is incompatible with sampling (sample\_count).

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/evm/endpoint/contracts#parameter-offset)

offset

integer

Offset row number to start (inclusive, first row means offset=0) returning results from. This together with 'limit' allows easy pagination through results in an incremental and efficient way. This parameter is incompatible with sampling (sample\_count).

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/evm/endpoint/contracts#parameter-query-id)

queryID

integer

required

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/evm/endpoint/contracts#parameter-sample-count)

sample\_count

integer

Number of rows to return from the result by sampling the data. This is useful when you want to get a uniform sample instead of the entire result. If the result has less than the sample count, the entire result is returned. Note that this will return a randomized sample, so not every call will return the same result. This parameter is incompatible with `offset`, `limit`, and `filters` parameters.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/evm/endpoint/contracts#parameter-sort-by)

sort\_by

string

Expression to define the order in which the results should be returned. This expression is similar to a SQL ORDER BY clause. More details about it in the Sorting section of the doc.

#### Response

200

application/json

OK

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/evm/endpoint/contracts#response-cancelled-at)

cancelled\_at

string

Timestamp of when the query execution was cancelled, if applicable.

Example:

`"2024-12-20T11:04:18.724658237Z"`

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/evm/endpoint/contracts#response-error)

error

object

In case the execution had an error, this object will contain the error details

Show child attributes

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/evm/endpoint/contracts#response-execution-ended-at)

execution\_ended\_at

string

Timestamp of when the query execution ended.

Example:

`"2024-12-20T11:04:18.724658237Z"`

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/evm/endpoint/contracts#response-execution-id)

execution\_id

string

Unique identifier for the execution of the query.

Example:

`"01HKZJ2683PHF9Q9PHHQ8FW4Q1"`

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/evm/endpoint/contracts#response-execution-started-at)

execution\_started\_at

string

Timestamp of when the query execution started.

Example:

`"2024-12-20T11:04:18.724658237Z"`

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/evm/endpoint/contracts#response-expires-at)

expires\_at

string

Timestamp of when the query result expires.

Example:

`"2024-12-20T11:04:18.724658237Z"`

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/evm/endpoint/contracts#response-is-execution-finished)

is\_execution\_finished

boolean

Whether the state of the query execution is terminal. This can be used for polling purposes.

Example:

`true`

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/evm/endpoint/contracts#response-next-offset)

next\_offset

integer

Offset that can be used to retrieve the next page of results.

Example:

`100`

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/evm/endpoint/contracts#response-next-uri)

next\_uri

string

URI that can be used to fetch the next page of results.

Example:

`"https://api.dune.com/api/v1/execution/01HKZJ2683PHF9Q9PHHQ8FW4Q1/results?offset=100&limit=100"`

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/evm/endpoint/contracts#response-query-id)

query\_id

integer

Unique identifier of the query.

Example:

`1234`

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/evm/endpoint/contracts#response-result)

result

object

The object containing the results and metadata of the query execution

Show child attributes

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/evm/endpoint/contracts#response-state)

state

string

The state of the query execution.

Example:

`"QUERY_STATE_COMPLETED"`

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/evm/endpoint/contracts#response-submitted-at)

submitted\_at

string

Timestamp of when the query was submitted.

Example:

`"2024-12-20T11:04:18.724658237Z"`

*   Query powering this endpoint can be found [here](https://dune.com/queries/3682939)
    
*   Scheduled to update daily (_AVS registrations happen once every few days normally_)

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/eigenlayer/endpoint/avs_metadata#column-descriptions)

Column Descriptions
====================================================================================================================

| Column | Description | Type |
| --- | --- | --- |
| avs\_name | Name of the Actively Validated Service (AVS) | string |
| avs\_contract\_address | Ethereum contract address of the AVS | string |
| website | Website URL of the AVS | string |
| twitter | Twitter link of the AVS | string |
| logo | URL path to the logo image of the AVS | string |
| description | Brief description of the AVS | string |

#### Headers

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/eigenlayer/endpoint/avs_metadata#parameter-x-dune-api-key)

X-Dune-Api-Key

string

required

API Key for the service

#### Query Parameters

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/eigenlayer/endpoint/avs_metadata#parameter-api-key)

api\_key

string

API Key, alternative to using the HTTP header X-Dune-Api-Key

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/eigenlayer/endpoint/avs_metadata#parameter-allow-partial-results)

allow\_partial\_results

boolean

This enables returning a query result that was too large and only a partial result is available. By default allow\_partial\_results is set to false and a failed state is returned.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/eigenlayer/endpoint/avs_metadata#parameter-columns)

columns

string

Specifies a comma-separated list of column names to return. If omitted, all columns are included. Tip: use this to limit the result to specific columns, reducing datapoints cost of the call.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/eigenlayer/endpoint/avs_metadata#parameter-filters)

filters

string

Expression to filter out rows from the results to return. This expression is similar to a SQL WHERE clause. More details about it in the Filtering section of the doc. This parameter is incompatible with sample\_count.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/eigenlayer/endpoint/avs_metadata#parameter-ignore-max-datapoints-per-request)

ignore\_max\_datapoints\_per\_request

boolean

There is a default 250,000 datapoints limit to make sure you don't accidentally spend all your credits in one call. To ignore the max limit, you can add ignore\_max\_datapoints\_per\_request=true

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/eigenlayer/endpoint/avs_metadata#parameter-limit)

limit

integer

Limit number of rows to return. This together with 'offset' allows easy pagination through results in an incremental and efficient way. This parameter is incompatible with sampling (sample\_count).

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/eigenlayer/endpoint/avs_metadata#parameter-offset)

offset

integer

Offset row number to start (inclusive, first row means offset=0) returning results from. This together with 'limit' allows easy pagination through results in an incremental and efficient way. This parameter is incompatible with sampling (sample\_count).

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/eigenlayer/endpoint/avs_metadata#parameter-query-id)

queryID

integer

required

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/eigenlayer/endpoint/avs_metadata#parameter-sample-count)

sample\_count

integer

Number of rows to return from the result by sampling the data. This is useful when you want to get a uniform sample instead of the entire result. If the result has less than the sample count, the entire result is returned. Note that this will return a randomized sample, so not every call will return the same result. This parameter is incompatible with `offset`, `limit`, and `filters` parameters.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/eigenlayer/endpoint/avs_metadata#parameter-sort-by)

sort\_by

string

Expression to define the order in which the results should be returned. This expression is similar to a SQL ORDER BY clause. More details about it in the Sorting section of the doc.

          "column_names": [\
            "Rank",\
            "Project",\

          ],

            "varchar",\
            "bigint"\

          "pending_time_millis": 1000,

          "row_count": 10,
          "total_result_set_bytes": 10000,
          "total_row_count": 1000
        },

        "update_type": "<string>"
      },

*   Query powering this endpoint can be found [here](https://dune.com/queries/3693850)
    
*   Scheduled to update 15 minutes
*   Apply [filters](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/executions/filtering)
     like WHERE, IN, AND/OR upon results
*   Use a combination of `sort_by` and `limit` to grab a subset of results, see [pagination](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/executions/pagination)
     and [sorting](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/executions/sorting)
     for more info

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/eigenlayer/endpoint/avs_metrics#column-descriptions)

Column Descriptions
===================================================================================================================

| Column | Description | Type |
| --- | --- | --- |
| avs\_name | Name of the Actively Validated Service (AVS) | string |
| avs\_contract\_address | Ethereum contract address of the AVS | string |
| num\_operators | Number of operators registered to the AVS | integer |
| total\_TVL | Total value locked across all strategies in the AVS | double |
| num\_stakers | Number of stakers currently staking to the AVS (via operators) | integer |
| cbETH\_TVL | Total value locked in cbETH strategy in the AVS | double |
| stETH\_TVL | Total value locked in stETH strategy in the AVS | double |
| rETH\_TVL | Total value locked in rETH strategy in the AVS | double |
| ETHx\_TVL | Total value locked in ETHx strategy in the AVS | double |
| ankrETH\_TVL | Total value locked in ankrETH strategy in the AVS | double |
| OETH\_TVL | Total value locked in OETH strategy in the AVS | double |
| osETH\_TVL | Total value locked in osETH strategy in the AVS | double |
| swETH\_TVL | Total value locked in swETH strategy in the AVS | double |
| wBETH\_TVL | Total value locked in wBETH strategy in the AVS | double |
| sfrxETH\_TVL | Total value locked in sfrxETH strategy in the AVS | double |
| lsETH\_TVL | Total value locked in lsETH strategy in the AVS | double |
| mETH\_TVL | Total value locked in mETH strategy in the AVS | double |
| beacon\_chain\_ETH\_TVL | Total value locked in Beacon Chain ETH strategy in the AVS | double |

#### Headers

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/eigenlayer/endpoint/avs_metrics#parameter-x-dune-api-key)

X-Dune-Api-Key

string

required

API Key for the service

#### Query Parameters

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/eigenlayer/endpoint/avs_metrics#parameter-api-key)

api\_key

string

API Key, alternative to using the HTTP header X-Dune-Api-Key

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/eigenlayer/endpoint/avs_metrics#parameter-allow-partial-results)

allow\_partial\_results

boolean

This enables returning a query result that was too large and only a partial result is available. By default allow\_partial\_results is set to false and a failed state is returned.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/eigenlayer/endpoint/avs_metrics#parameter-columns)

columns

string

Specifies a comma-separated list of column names to return. If omitted, all columns are included. Tip: use this to limit the result to specific columns, reducing datapoints cost of the call.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/eigenlayer/endpoint/avs_metrics#parameter-filters)

filters

string

Expression to filter out rows from the results to return. This expression is similar to a SQL WHERE clause. More details about it in the Filtering section of the doc. This parameter is incompatible with sample\_count.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/eigenlayer/endpoint/avs_metrics#parameter-ignore-max-datapoints-per-request)

ignore\_max\_datapoints\_per\_request

boolean

There is a default 250,000 datapoints limit to make sure you don't accidentally spend all your credits in one call. To ignore the max limit, you can add ignore\_max\_datapoints\_per\_request=true

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/eigenlayer/endpoint/avs_metrics#parameter-limit)

limit

integer

Limit number of rows to return. This together with 'offset' allows easy pagination through results in an incremental and efficient way. This parameter is incompatible with sampling (sample\_count).

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/eigenlayer/endpoint/avs_metrics#parameter-offset)

offset

integer

Offset row number to start (inclusive, first row means offset=0) returning results from. This together with 'limit' allows easy pagination through results in an incremental and efficient way. This parameter is incompatible with sampling (sample\_count).

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/eigenlayer/endpoint/avs_metrics#parameter-query-id)

queryID

integer

required

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/eigenlayer/endpoint/avs_metrics#parameter-sample-count)

sample\_count

integer

Number of rows to return from the result by sampling the data. This is useful when you want to get a uniform sample instead of the entire result. If the result has less than the sample count, the entire result is returned. Note that this will return a randomized sample, so not every call will return the same result. This parameter is incompatible with `offset`, `limit`, and `filters` parameters.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/eigenlayer/endpoint/avs_metrics#parameter-sort-by)

sort\_by

string

Expression to define the order in which the results should be returned. This expression is similar to a SQL ORDER BY clause. More details about it in the Sorting section of the doc.

#### Response

200

application/json

OK

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/eigenlayer/endpoint/avs_metrics#response-cancelled-at)

cancelled\_at

string

Timestamp of when the query execution was cancelled, if applicable.

Example:

`"2024-12-20T11:04:18.724658237Z"`

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/eigenlayer/endpoint/avs_metrics#response-error)

error

object

In case the execution had an error, this object will contain the error details

Show child attributes

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/eigenlayer/endpoint/avs_metrics#response-execution-ended-at)

execution\_ended\_at

string

Timestamp of when the query execution ended.

Example:

`"2024-12-20T11:04:18.724658237Z"`

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/eigenlayer/endpoint/avs_metrics#response-execution-id)

execution\_id

string

Unique identifier for the execution of the query.

Example:

`"01HKZJ2683PHF9Q9PHHQ8FW4Q1"`

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/eigenlayer/endpoint/avs_metrics#response-execution-started-at)

execution\_started\_at

string

Timestamp of when the query execution started.

Example:

`"2024-12-20T11:04:18.724658237Z"`

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/eigenlayer/endpoint/avs_metrics#response-expires-at)

expires\_at

string

Timestamp of when the query result expires.

Example:

`"2024-12-20T11:04:18.724658237Z"`

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/eigenlayer/endpoint/avs_metrics#response-is-execution-finished)

is\_execution\_finished

boolean

Whether the state of the query execution is terminal. This can be used for polling purposes.

Example:

`true`

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/eigenlayer/endpoint/avs_metrics#response-next-offset)

next\_offset

integer

Offset that can be used to retrieve the next page of results.

Example:

`100`

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/eigenlayer/endpoint/avs_metrics#response-next-uri)

next\_uri

string

URI that can be used to fetch the next page of results.

Example:

`"https://api.dune.com/api/v1/execution/01HKZJ2683PHF9Q9PHHQ8FW4Q1/results?offset=100&limit=100"`

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/eigenlayer/endpoint/avs_metrics#response-query-id)

query\_id

integer

Unique identifier of the query.

Example:

`1234`

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/eigenlayer/endpoint/avs_metrics#response-result)

result

object

The object containing the results and metadata of the query execution

Show child attributes

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/eigenlayer/endpoint/avs_metrics#response-state)

state

string

The state of the query execution.

Example:

`"QUERY_STATE_COMPLETED"`

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/eigenlayer/endpoint/avs_metrics#response-submitted-at)

submitted\_at

string

Timestamp of when the query was submitted.

Example:

`"2024-12-20T11:04:18.724658237Z"`

Complete Workflow

Copy

Ask AI

curl -X POST "https://api.dune.com/api/v1/sql/execute" \
      -H "Content-Type: application/json" \
      -H "X-Dune-Api-Key: YOUR_API_KEY" \
      -d '{
        "sql": "SELECT * FROM dex.trades WHERE block_time > now() - interval '\''1 day'\'' LIMIT 10",
        "performance": "medium"
      }'

> Run arbitrary SQL queries via API. This endpoint allows you to execute SQL directly without first creating a query object, perfect for dynamic analysis and automated workflows.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/executions/endpoint/execute-sql#pricing)

Pricing
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

This endpoint is **usage-based** and consumes credits based on the computational resources used during execution.

cURL

Python

JavaScript

Complete Workflow

Copy

Ask AI

    curl -X POST "https://api.dune.com/api/v1/sql/execute" \
      -H "Content-Type: application/json" \
      -H "X-Dune-Api-Key: YOUR_API_KEY" \
      -d '{
        "sql": "SELECT * FROM dex.trades WHERE block_time > now() - interval '\''1 day'\'' LIMIT 10",
        "performance": "medium"
      }'
    

Copy

Ask AI

    {
      "execution_id": "01HKZJ2683PHF9Q9PHHQ8FW4Q1",
      "state": "QUERY_STATE_PENDING"
    }
    

#### Headers

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/executions/endpoint/execute-sql#parameter-x-dune-api-key)

X-Dune-Api-Key

string

required

API Key for the service

#### Query Parameters

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/executions/endpoint/execute-sql#parameter-api-key)

api\_key

string

Alternative to using the X-Dune-Api-Key header

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/executions/endpoint/execute-sql#parameter-performance)

performance

enum<string>

The performance engine tier the execution will be run on. Can be either `medium` or `large`. Credits are consumed based on actual compute resources used. Medium is the default, large provides more resources for complex queries.

Available options:

`medium`,

`large`

#### Body

\*/\* · string

Raw SQL query to execute

The body is of type `string`.

#### Response

200

application/json

OK

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/executions/endpoint/execute-sql#response-execution-id)

execution\_id

string

Example:

`"01HKZJ2683PHF9Q9PHHQ8FW4Q1"`

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/executions/endpoint/execute-sql#response-state)

state

string

Example:

`"QUERY_STATE_PENDING"`

# Dune Farcaster Endpoints - Dune Docs

[Skip to main content](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/farcaster/introduction#content-area)

[Dune Docs home page![light logo](https://mintcdn.com/dune/uyJ-jHeSRFvNrzyu/logo/dune-logo-light.png?fit=max&auto=format&n=uyJ-jHeSRFvNrzyu&q=85&s=fbdf0e7e6fabc31e49afcdb53cb5e774)![dark logo](https://mintcdn.com/dune/uyJ-jHeSRFvNrzyu/logo/dune-logo-dark.png?fit=max&auto=format&n=uyJ-jHeSRFvNrzyu&q=85&s=767370d661596e21a7b3a4525d50d77e)](https://dune.com/)

Search...

⌘K

Search...

Navigation

Farcaster

Dune Farcaster Endpoints

[Get Started](https://docs.dune.com/home)
[Analytics Studio](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/overview)
[Query Engine](https://docs.dune.com/query-engine/overview)
[Data Catalog](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/overview)
[Analytics API](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/overview/introduction)
[Datashare](https://docs.dune.com/datashare/datashare)
[Catalyst](https://docs.dune.com/catalyst/overview)

While you can create/use any query as an API endpoint, we’ve defined three popular queries as preset endpoints (so you don’t need to worry about executions or editing SQL). You should use these endpoints to provide better data to inform your algorithms, recommendations, or UI elements.

[Trending Farcaster Users\
------------------------\
\
Get trending users, based on farcaster engagement and onchain activity](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/farcaster/endpoint/farcaster_users)
[Trending Farcaster Channels\
---------------------------\
\
Get trending channels, based on user tiers, onchain activity, and engagement.](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/farcaster/endpoint/farcaster_channels)
[Trending Farcaster Memecoins\
----------------------------\
\
Get trending memecoins, based on engagement, holders, liquidity, volume, and more.](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/farcaster/endpoint/farcaster_memecoins)

[Farcaster Channels](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/farcaster/endpoint/farcaster_channels)

Column Descriptions
===============================================================================================================================

| Column | Description | Type |
| --- | --- | --- |
| avs\_contract\_address | Ethereum contract address of the AVS | string |
| avs\_name | Name of the Actively Validated Service (AVS) | string |
| avs\_website | Website URL of the AVS | string |
| operator\_contract\_address | Ethereum contract address of the operator | string |
| operator\_name | Name of the operator | string |
| operator\_website | Website URL of the operator | string |
| registered\_time | Timestamp of when the operator registered to the AVS | string |

#### Headers

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/eigenlayer/endpoint/operator_to_avs_mapping#parameter-x-dune-api-key)

X-Dune-Api-Key

string

required

API Key for the service

#### Query Parameters

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/eigenlayer/endpoint/operator_to_avs_mapping#parameter-api-key)

api\_key

string

API Key, alternative to using the HTTP header X-Dune-Api-Key

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/eigenlayer/endpoint/operator_to_avs_mapping#parameter-allow-partial-results)

allow\_partial\_results

boolean

This enables returning a query result that was too large and only a partial result is available. By default allow\_partial\_results is set to false and a failed state is returned.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/eigenlayer/endpoint/operator_to_avs_mapping#parameter-columns)

columns

string

Specifies a comma-separated list of column names to return. If omitted, all columns are included. Tip: use this to limit the result to specific columns, reducing datapoints cost of the call.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/eigenlayer/endpoint/operator_to_avs_mapping#parameter-filters)

filters

string

Expression to filter out rows from the results to return. This expression is similar to a SQL WHERE clause. More details about it in the Filtering section of the doc. This parameter is incompatible with sample\_count.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/eigenlayer/endpoint/operator_to_avs_mapping#parameter-ignore-max-datapoints-per-request)

ignore\_max\_datapoints\_per\_request

boolean

There is a default 250,000 datapoints limit to make sure you don't accidentally spend all your credits in one call. To ignore the max limit, you can add ignore\_max\_datapoints\_per\_request=true

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/eigenlayer/endpoint/operator_to_avs_mapping#parameter-limit)

limit

integer

Limit number of rows to return. This together with 'offset' allows easy pagination through results in an incremental and efficient way. This parameter is incompatible with sampling (sample\_count).

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/eigenlayer/endpoint/operator_to_avs_mapping#parameter-offset)

offset

integer

Offset row number to start (inclusive, first row means offset=0) returning results from. This together with 'limit' allows easy pagination through results in an incremental and efficient way. This parameter is incompatible with sampling (sample\_count).

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/eigenlayer/endpoint/operator_to_avs_mapping#parameter-query-id)

queryID

integer

required

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/eigenlayer/endpoint/operator_to_avs_mapping#parameter-sample-count)

sample\_count

integer

Number of rows to return from the result by sampling the data. This is useful when you want to get a uniform sample instead of the entire result. If the result has less than the sample count, the entire result is returned. Note that this will return a randomized sample, so not every call will return the same result. This parameter is incompatible with `offset`, `limit`, and `filters` parameters.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/eigenlayer/endpoint/operator_to_avs_mapping#parameter-sort-by)

sort\_by

string

Expression to define the order in which the results should be returned. This expression is similar to a SQL ORDER BY clause. More details about it in the Sorting section of the doc.

#### Response

200

application/json

OK

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/eigenlayer/endpoint/operator_to_avs_mapping#response-cancelled-at)

cancelled\_at

string

Timestamp of when the query execution was cancelled, if applicable.

Example:

`"2024-12-20T11:04:18.724658237Z"`

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/eigenlayer/endpoint/operator_to_avs_mapping#response-error)

error

object

In case the execution had an error, this object will contain the error details

Show child attributes

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/eigenlayer/endpoint/operator_to_avs_mapping#response-execution-ended-at)

execution\_ended\_at

string

Timestamp of when the query execution ended.

Example:

`"2024-12-20T11:04:18.724658237Z"`

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/eigenlayer/endpoint/operator_to_avs_mapping#response-execution-id)

execution\_id

string

Unique identifier for the execution of the query.

Example:

`"01HKZJ2683PHF9Q9PHHQ8FW4Q1"`

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/eigenlayer/endpoint/operator_to_avs_mapping#response-execution-started-at)

execution\_started\_at

string

Timestamp of when the query execution started.

Example:

`"2024-12-20T11:04:18.724658237Z"`

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/eigenlayer/endpoint/operator_to_avs_mapping#response-expires-at)

expires\_at

string

Timestamp of when the query result expires.

Example:

`"2024-12-20T11:04:18.724658237Z"`

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/eigenlayer/endpoint/operator_to_avs_mapping#response-is-execution-finished)

is\_execution\_finished

boolean

Whether the state of the query execution is terminal. This can be used for polling purposes.

Example:

`true`

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/eigenlayer/endpoint/operator_to_avs_mapping#response-next-offset)

next\_offset

integer

Offset that can be used to retrieve the next page of results.

Example:

`100`

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/eigenlayer/endpoint/operator_to_avs_mapping#response-next-uri)

next\_uri

string

URI that can be used to fetch the next page of results.

Example:

`"https://api.dune.com/api/v1/execution/01HKZJ2683PHF9Q9PHHQ8FW4Q1/results?offset=100&limit=100"`

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/eigenlayer/endpoint/operator_to_avs_mapping#response-query-id)

query\_id

integer

Unique identifier of the query.

Example:

`1234`

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/eigenlayer/endpoint/operator_to_avs_mapping#response-result)

result

object

The object containing the results and metadata of the query execution

Show child attributes

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/eigenlayer/endpoint/operator_to_avs_mapping#response-state)

state

string

The state of the query execution.

Example:

`"QUERY_STATE_COMPLETED"`

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/eigenlayer/endpoint/operator_to_avs_mapping#response-submitted-at)

submitted\_at

string

Timestamp of when the query was submitted.

Example:

`"2024-12-20T11:04:18.724658237Z"`

*   Query powering this endpoint can be found [here](https://dune.com/queries/3685928)
    
*   Scheduled to update every 15 minutes
*   Apply [filters](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/executions/filtering)
     like WHERE, IN, AND/OR upon results
*   Use a combination of `sort_by` and `limit` to grab a subset of results, see [pagination](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/executions/pagination)
     and [sorting](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/executions/sorting)
     for more info

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/eigenlayer/endpoint/operator_metrics#column-descriptions)

Column Descriptions
========================================================================================================================

| Column | Description | Type |
| --- | --- | --- |
| operator\_name | Name of the operator | string |
| operator\_contract\_address | Ethereum contract address of the operator | string |
| total\_TVL | Total value locked in the operator across all strategies (except for EIGEN token) | double |
| num\_stakers | Number of stakers currently staking to the operator | double |
| cbETH\_TVL | Total value locked in cbETH strategy in the operator | double |
| stETH\_TVL | Total value locked in stETH strategy in the operator | double |
| rETH\_TVL | Total value locked in rETH strategy in the operator | double |
| ETHx\_TVL | Total value locked in ETHx strategy in the operator | double |
| ankrETH\_TVL | Total value locked in ankrETH strategy in the operator | double |
| OETH\_TVL | Total value locked in OETH strategy in the operator | double |
| osETH\_TVL | Total value locked in osETH strategy in the operator | double |
| swETH\_TVL | Total value locked in swETH strategy in the operator | double |
| wBETH\_TVL | Total value locked in wBETH strategy in the operator | double |
| sfrxETH\_TVL | Total value locked in sfrxETH strategy in the operator | double |
| lsETH\_TVL | Total value locked in lsETH strategy in the operator | double |
| mETH\_TVL | Total value locked in mETH strategy in the operator | double |
| beacon\_chain\_ETH\_TVL | Total value locked in Beacon Chain ETH strategy in the operator | double |
| EIGEN\_TVL | Total value locked in EIGEN strategy in the operator | double |

Number of rows to return from the result by sampling the data. This is useful when you want to get a uniform sample instead of the entire result. If the result has less than the sample count, the entire result is returned. Note that this will return a randomized sample, so not every call will return the same result. Expression to define the order in which the results should be returned. This expression is similar to a SQL ORDER BY clause. More details about it in the Sorting section of the doc.

You must pass the `execution_id` obtained from making an [execute query](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/executions/endpoint/execute-query)
 POST request. The result returns a boolean for whether the execution is successfully canceled.

# Upsert Materialized View - Dune Docs

[Skip to main content](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/materialized-views/create#content-area)

Materialized Views

Upsert Materialized View

[Get Started](https://docs.dune.com/home)
[Analytics Studio](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/overview)
[Query Engine](https://docs.dune.com/query-engine/overview)
[Data Catalog](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/overview)
[Analytics API](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/overview/introduction)
[Datashare](https://docs.dune.com/datashare/datashare)
[Catalyst](https://docs.dune.com/catalyst/overview)

This upserts (create or replace) a materialized view from an existing query

cURL

Copy

Ask AI

    curl --request POST \
      --url https://api.dune.com/api/v1/materialized-views \
      --header 'Content-Type: */*' \
      --header 'X-Dune-Api-Key: <x-dune-api-key>' \
      --data '{
      "cron_expression": "<string>",
      "expires_at": "<string>",
      "is_private": true,
      "name": "<string>",
      "performance": "<string>",
      "query_id": 123
    }'

200

400

401

404

500

Copy

Ask AI

    {
      "execution_id": "01HZ065JVE23C23FM2HKWQP2RT",
      "name": "dune.dune.result_erc_20_token_summary"
    }

POST

/

v1

/

materialized-views

Try it

This upserts (create or replace) a materialized view from an existing query

cURL

Copy

Ask AI

    curl --request POST \
      --url https://api.dune.com/api/v1/materialized-views \
      --header 'Content-Type: */*' \
      --header 'X-Dune-Api-Key: <x-dune-api-key>' \
      --data '{
      "cron_expression": "<string>",
      "expires_at": "<string>",
      "is_private": true,
      "name": "<string>",
      "performance": "<string>",
      "query_id": 123
    }'

200

400

401

404

500

Copy

Ask AI

    {
      "execution_id": "01HZ065JVE23C23FM2HKWQP2RT",
      "name": "dune.dune.result_erc_20_token_summary"
    }

*   This endpoint will create a new matview if none exists for the given query ID, or update an existing one if the query ID matches.
*   It will fail to create a matview with the same name as an existing one, but for a different query ID
*   The name of the matview is just the last part of the matview, not including `dune.<your_team>.` and must be prefixed with `result_`
*   The `cron_expression` parameter must be passed in as a valid 5 section cron expression. [See here](https://crontab.guru/)
     for how to write them.

*   The cron expression interval must be at least 15 minutes and at most weekly

#### Headers

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/materialized-views/create#parameter-x-dune-api-key)

X-Dune-Api-Key

string

required

API Key for the service

#### Path Parameters

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/materialized-views/create#parameter-name)

name

string

required

Matview Name

#### Query Parameters

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/materialized-views/create#parameter-api-key)

api\_key

string

API Key, alternative to using the HTTP header X-Dune-Api-Key

#### Body

\*/\*

MatviewsUpsertRequest

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/materialized-views/create#body-cron-expression)

cron\_expression

string

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/materialized-views/create#body-expires-at)

expires\_at

string

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/materialized-views/create#body-is-private)

is\_private

boolean

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/materialized-views/create#body-name)

name

string

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/materialized-views/create#body-performance)

performance

string

Performance level of the refresh. Available options: `medium`, `large`

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/materialized-views/create#body-query-id)

query\_id

integer

#### Response

200

application/json

OK

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/materialized-views/create#response-execution-id)

execution\_id

string

Unique identifier for the execution triggered to refresh the materialized view

Example:

`"01HZ065JVE23C23FM2HKWQP2RT"`

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/materialized-views/create#response-name)

name

string

Unique identifier for the materialized view

Example:

`"dune.dune.result_erc_20_token_summary"`

# Overview - Dune Docs

[Skip to main content](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/executions/execution-object#content-area)

[Dune Docs home page![light logo](https://mintcdn.com/dune/uyJ-jHeSRFvNrzyu/logo/dune-logo-light.png?fit=max&auto=format&n=uyJ-jHeSRFvNrzyu&q=85&s=fbdf0e7e6fabc31e49afcdb53cb5e774)![dark logo](https://mintcdn.com/dune/uyJ-jHeSRFvNrzyu/logo/dune-logo-dark.png?fit=max&auto=format&n=uyJ-jHeSRFvNrzyu&q=85&s=767370d661596e21a7b3a4525d50d77e)](https://dune.com/)

Executions and Results

Overview

[Get Started](https://docs.dune.com/home)
[Analytics Studio](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/overview)
[Query Engine](https://docs.dune.com/query-engine/overview)
[Data Catalog](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/overview)
[Analytics API](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/overview/introduction)
[Datashare](https://docs.dune.com/datashare/datashare)
[Catalyst](https://docs.dune.com/catalyst/overview)

On this page

*   [Queries, Executions, and Results](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/executions/execution-object#queries%2C-executions%2C-and-results)
    
*   [Query Filters vs. Execution Parameters](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/executions/execution-object#query-filters-vs-execution-parameters)
    
*   [Choosing Between Options](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/executions/execution-object#choosing-between-options)
    
*   [Endpoints](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/executions/execution-object#endpoints)
    

The executions and results endpoints facilitate the execution of saved queries, retrieval of results in various formats, and management of query executions.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/executions/execution-object#queries%2C-executions%2C-and-results)

Queries, Executions, and Results
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Results are linked to executions, and executions are tied to queries. Each execution has an `execution_id`. An `execution_id` is generated when you initiate the execution of a query through the [execute query](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/executions/endpoint/execute-query)
 endpoint. Unlike a `query_id`, which identifies a specific query, an `execution_id` represents a particular execution of that query. With an `execution_id`, you can monitor the execution’s status using the [check status](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/executions/endpoint/get-execution-status)
 endpoint. The status can be one of the following: pending, success, or failure. If an execution is successful, you can get the result using [get result](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/executions/endpoint/get-execution-result)
. Results are saved and can be retrieved multiple times. Results data from an execution are stored with an expiration date of 90 days (subject to change). This is visible on the API response on the “expires\_at” field in the execution status and results json body (not on the CSV endpoint).

*   Save your `execution_id` for later use without re-executing.
*   Use the [get latest query result](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/executions/endpoint/get-query-result)
     endpoint to fetch the most recent result.
*   Understanding the differences and relationships between query results filters, schedules, executions, and params is crucial. Further details are provided below.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/executions/execution-object#query-filters-vs-execution-parameters)

Query Filters vs. Execution Parameters
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Two primary methods exist for fetching data from the Dune API while applying specific conditions: **Option 1**: Utilize filters with the latest query result and employ schedules to maintain data freshness.

1.  Obtain the `query_id`.
2.  Use [get latest query result](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/executions/endpoint/get-query-result)
     endpoint to access the most recent results.
3.  Apply [filters](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/executions/filtering)
     for desired data subsets.
4.  Implement schedules for maintaining data freshness.

**Option 2**: Execute a query with parameters to retrieve the desired subset of data.

1.  Obtain the `query_id`.
2.  Use [execute query](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/executions/endpoint/execute-query)
     endpoint with parameters to trigger fresh execution.
3.  Grab the `execution_id` from the response.
4.  Fetch results via [get execution result](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/executions/endpoint/get-execution-result)
     endpoint using the `execution_id`.

### 

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/executions/execution-object#choosing-between-options)

Choosing Between Options

*   Option 1 offers speed, as it builds upon existing results with filters. Use it when quick results are essential.
*   Option 2 allows dynamic parameter passing for fresh executions. Employ it when real-time parameterization is required.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/executions/execution-object#endpoints)

Endpoints
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Below is an overview of each endpoint, providing a high-level understanding of their functionalities.

| Endpoint Title | Endpoint | Description |
| --- | --- | --- |
| [Cancel Execution](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/executions/endpoint/cancel-execution) | `POST /v1/execution/{execution_id}/cancel` | Cancels an ongoing query execution. Requires the `execution_id`. Returns a success boolean. |
| [Execute Query](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/executions/endpoint/execute-query) | `POST /v1/query/{query_id}/execute` | Triggers an execution based on the `query_id`. Returns a `execution_id`. |
| [Get Execution Status](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/executions/endpoint/get-execution-status) | `GET /v1/execution/{execution_id}/status` | Provides the status of a query execution given an `execution_id`. |
| [Get Execution Result in CSV](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/executions/endpoint/get-execution-result-csv) | `GET /v1/execution/{execution_id}/results/csv` | Retrieves the status, metadata, and results in CSV format. Includes data retention and limit information. |
| [Get Execution Result](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/executions/endpoint/get-execution-result) | `GET /v1/execution/{execution_id}/results` | Fetches the execution status, metadata, and results in JSON format. Similar data handling as CSV endpoint. |
| [Get Latest Query Result in CSV](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/executions/endpoint/get-query-result-csv) | `GET /v1/query/{query_id}/results/csv` | Returns the latest results of a query in CSV format, irrespective of the execution method. Queries must be public or owned. |
| [Get Latest Query Result](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/executions/endpoint/get-query-result) | `GET /v1/query/{query_id}/results` | Similar to the CSV endpoint but returns results in JSON format. Follows the same access and data limit policies. |

Execute query and get result in one call

If you are using the [Python SDK](https://github.com/duneanalytics/dune-client/tree/d2195b2a9577e2dcae5d2600cb3eddce20987f38)
, you can directly execute and fetch result in one function call, like below:

Use `run_query` to get result in JSON, `run_query_csv` to get result in CSV format, and `run_query_dataframe` to get result in Pandas dataframe

Python SDK

Copy

Ask AI

    
    import json
    from dune_client.types import QueryParameter
    from dune_client.client import DuneClient
    from dune_client.query import QueryBase
    
    # setup Dune Python client
    dune = DuneClient()
    
    query = QueryBase(
        name="Sample Query",
        query_id=1215383,
    )
    
    result = dune.run_query(
        query = query,
        performance = 'large' # optionally define which tier to run the execution on (default is "medium")
    )
    
    # go over the results returned
    for row in result.result.rows: 
        print (row) # as an example we print the rows
If the query has parameters and you don’t add them in your API call, it will just run with the default params. You may add query parameters as part of the POST params data. You can choose to include a `performance` parameter, by default it will use the “medium” performance tier. Credits are consumed based on actual compute resources used. “large” tier provides more resources for complex queries. Returns an execution\_id associated with the triggered query execution and the state of the execution.

cURL

Python SDK

Python

Javascript

Go

PHP

Java

Copy

Ask AI

    curl -X POST "https://api.dune.com/api/v1/query/{{query_id}}/execute"   \
      -H "X-Dune-API-Key: {{api_key}}"                                       \
      -H "Content-Type: application/json"                                   \
      -d '{"query_parameters": {"param1":24}, "performance": "large"}'
    

#### Headers

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/executions/endpoint/execute-query#parameter-x-dune-api-key)

X-Dune-Api-Key

string

required

API Key for the service

#### Path Parameters

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/executions/endpoint/execute-query#parameter-query-id)

query\_id

integer

required

Unique identifier of the query

#### Query Parameters

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/executions/endpoint/execute-query#parameter-api-key)

api\_key

string

Alternative to using the X-Dune-Api-Key header

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/executions/endpoint/execute-query#parameter-performance)

performance

enum<string>

The performance engine tier the execution will be run on. Can be either `medium` or `large`. Credits are consumed based on actual compute resources used. Medium is the default, large provides more resources for complex queries.

Available options:

`medium`,

`large`

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/executions/endpoint/execute-query#parameter-query-parameters)

query\_parameters

string

SQL Query parameters in json key-value pairs. Each parameter is to be provided in key-value pairs. This enables you to execute a parameterized query with the provided values for your parameter keys. Partial submission of parameters is allowed. For example, if the query expects three parameters and you only pass in two, the third one will automatically use its default value as defined in the Query Parameter Editor page.

#### Response

200

application/json

OK

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/executions/endpoint/execute-query#response-execution-id)

execution\_id

string

Example:

`"01HKZJ2683PHF9Q9PHHQ8FW4Q1"`

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/executions/endpoint/execute-query#response-state)

state

string

Example:

`"QUERY_STATE_PENDING"`
