*   Query can be found [here](https://dune.com/queries/3575029)
    
*   Chains included are: all [EVM chains on Dune](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/markets/endpoint/data-catalog/evm/overview)
    
*   Scheduled to update every day (23:30 UTC)
*   You can apply [filters](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/executions/filtering)
     like WHERE, IN, AND/OR upon results

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/markets/endpoint/marketplace_marketshare#use-cases)

Use Cases
========================================================================================================

*   Recommend trending or emerging marketplaces by tracking shifts in the market share over time.
*   Feed into a marketing ROI tracker to assess campaign impacts on marketplace market share.
*   Build a competitive analysis tool to monitor marketplaces and sectors’ market share over time.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/markets/endpoint/marketplace_marketshare#column-descriptions)

Column Descriptions
============================================================================================================================

| Column | Description | Type |
| --- | --- | --- |
| time | Date of the marketshare data | string |
| market | Sector identifier: ‘dex’ or ‘nft’ | string |
| blockchain | The blockchain where the marketplace operates on | string |
| project | Specific DEX or NFT marketplace name | string |
| version | Contract version of the marketplace protocol, e.g. ‘v2’ | string |
| volume\_usd | USD volume traded on the marketplace | double |
| trades | Number of trades on the marketplace | int |

#### Headers

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/markets/endpoint/marketplace_marketshare#parameter-x-dune-api-key)

X-Dune-Api-Key

string

required

API Key for the service

#### Path Parameters

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/markets/endpoint/marketplace_marketshare#parameter-market)

market

string

required

Sector of the marketshare, either 'dex' or 'nft'

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/markets/endpoint/marketplace_marketshare#parameter-chain)

chain

string

required

Chain name (use Dune namespace, e.g. ethereum, solana, bnb, polygon, etc)

#### Query Parameters

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/markets/endpoint/marketplace_marketshare#parameter-api-key)

api\_key

string

API Key, alternative to using the HTTP header X-Dune-Api-Key

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/markets/endpoint/marketplace_marketshare#parameter-allow-partial-results)

allow\_partial\_results

boolean

This enables returning a query result that was too large and only a partial result is available. By default allow\_partial\_results is set to false and a failed state is returned.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/markets/endpoint/marketplace_marketshare#parameter-columns)

columns

string

Specifies a comma-separated list of column names to return. If omitted, all columns are included. Tip: use this to limit the result to specific columns, reducing datapoints cost of the call.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/markets/endpoint/marketplace_marketshare#parameter-filters)

filters

string

Expression to filter out rows from the results to return. This expression is similar to a SQL WHERE clause. More details about it in the Filtering section of the doc. This parameter is incompatible with sample\_count.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/markets/endpoint/marketplace_marketshare#parameter-ignore-max-datapoints-per-request)

ignore\_max\_datapoints\_per\_request

boolean

There is a default 250,000 datapoints limit to make sure you don't accidentally spend all your credits in one call. To ignore the max limit, you can add ignore\_max\_datapoints\_per\_request=true

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/markets/endpoint/marketplace_marketshare#parameter-limit)

limit

integer

Limit number of rows to return. This together with 'offset' allows easy pagination through results in an incremental and efficient way. This parameter is incompatible with sampling (sample\_count).

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/markets/endpoint/marketplace_marketshare#parameter-offset)

offset

integer

Offset row number to start (inclusive, first row means offset=0) returning results from. This together with 'limit' allows easy pagination through results in an incremental and efficient way. This parameter is incompatible with sampling (sample\_count).

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/markets/endpoint/marketplace_marketshare#parameter-query-id)

queryID

integer

required

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/markets/endpoint/marketplace_marketshare#parameter-sample-count)

sample\_count

integer

Number of rows to return from the result by sampling the data. This is useful when you want to get a uniform sample instead of the entire result. If the result has less than the sample count, the entire result is returned. Note that this will return a randomized sample, so not every call will return the same result. This parameter is incompatible with `offset`, `limit`, and `filters` parameters.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/markets/endpoint/marketplace_marketshare#parameter-sort-by)

sort\_by

string

Expression to define the order in which the results should be returned. This expression is similar to a SQL ORDER BY clause. More details about it in the Sorting section of the doc.

#### Response

200

application/json

OK

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/markets/endpoint/marketplace_marketshare#response-cancelled-at)

cancelled\_at

string

Timestamp of when the query execution was cancelled, if applicable.

Example:

`"2024-12-20T11:04:18.724658237Z"`

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/markets/endpoint/marketplace_marketshare#response-error)

error

object

In case the execution had an error, this object will contain the error details

Show child attributes

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/markets/endpoint/marketplace_marketshare#response-execution-ended-at)

execution\_ended\_at

string

Timestamp of when the query execution ended.

Example:

`"2024-12-20T11:04:18.724658237Z"`

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/markets/endpoint/marketplace_marketshare#response-execution-id)

execution\_id

string

Unique identifier for the execution of the query.

Example:

`"01HKZJ2683PHF9Q9PHHQ8FW4Q1"`

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/markets/endpoint/marketplace_marketshare#response-execution-started-at)

execution\_started\_at

string

Timestamp of when the query execution started.

Example:

`"2024-12-20T11:04:18.724658237Z"`

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/markets/endpoint/marketplace_marketshare#response-expires-at)

expires\_at

string

Timestamp of when the query result expires.

Example:

`"2024-12-20T11:04:18.724658237Z"`

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/markets/endpoint/marketplace_marketshare#response-is-execution-finished)

is\_execution\_finished

boolean

Whether the state of the query execution is terminal. This can be used for polling purposes.

Example:

`true`

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/markets/endpoint/marketplace_marketshare#response-next-offset)

next\_offset

integer

Offset that can be used to retrieve the next page of results.

Example:

`100`

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/markets/endpoint/marketplace_marketshare#response-next-uri)

next\_uri

string

URI that can be used to fetch the next page of results.

Example:

`"https://api.dune.com/api/v1/execution/01HKZJ2683PHF9Q9PHHQ8FW4Q1/results?offset=100&limit=100"`

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/markets/endpoint/marketplace_marketshare#response-query-id)

query\_id

integer

Unique identifier of the query.

Example:

`1234`

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/markets/endpoint/marketplace_marketshare#response-result)

result

object

The object containing the results and metadata of the query execution

Show child attributes

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/markets/endpoint/marketplace_marketshare#response-state)

state

string

The state of the query execution.

Example:

`"QUERY_STATE_COMPLETED"`

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/markets/endpoint/marketplace_marketshare#response-submitted-at)

submitted\_at

string

Timestamp of when the query was submitted.

Example:

`"2024-12-20T11:04:18.724658237Z"`

*   Query can be found [here](https://dune.com/queries/3662242)
    
*   Scheduled to update every 30 minutes
*   You can apply [filters](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/executions/filtering)
     like WHERE, IN, AND/OR upon results
*   Learn about memecoins and categories [in this article](https://read.cryptodatabytes.com/p/a-social-and-financial-study-of-memecoins)
    

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/farcaster/endpoint/farcaster_memecoins#use-cases)

Use Cases
======================================================================================================

*   Recommend trending memecoins based on farcaster engagement, liquidity, volume, or other onchain activity

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/farcaster/endpoint/farcaster_memecoins#column-descriptions)

Column Descriptions
==========================================================================================================================

Learn more about the score and methodology [in this article](https://read.cryptodatabytes.com/p/a-social-and-financial-study-of-memecoins)
.

| Column | Description | Type |
| --- | --- | --- |
| word\_raw | Ticker symbol of the token | string |
| related\_symbol | Any symbol or word that is related to the token (i.e. the degen hat or higher arrow) | string |
| token\_contract\_address | Contract address of the token | string |
| blockchain | Blockchain on which the token is deployed | string |
| deployed\_days\_ago | Number of days since the token was deployed | integer |
| social\_score | Social score of the token | integer |
| financial\_score | Financial score of the token | integer |
| meme\_category | Category of meme based off of social and financial score values | string |
| casters | Number of users who have casted the token ticker | integer |
| casters\_wow | Change in the number of casters week over week | integer |
| percent\_recipient\_casters | Percentage of casters this week that have received the token before | integer |
| percent\_recipient\_wow | Change in the percentage of recipient casters week over week | integer |
| recipient\_casters | Number of casters this week that have received the token before | integer |
| recipient\_casters\_wow | Change in the number of recipient casters week over week | integer |
| casts | Number of times the token ticker has been casted | integer |
| casts\_wow | Change in the number of casts week over week | integer |
| channels | Number of channels the token ticker has been casted in | integer |
| channels\_wow | Change in the number of channels week over week | integer |
| activity\_level | Activity level of the token | integer |
| activity\_wow | Change in the activity level week over week | integer |
| total\_supply | Total supply of the token | integer |
| fdv | Fully diluted valuation of the token | integer |
| median\_price | Median price of the token | integer |
| day\_pnl | Profit and loss of the token price in the last 24 hours | integer |
| week\_pnl | Profit and loss of the token price in the last 7 days | integer |
| month\_pnl | Profit and loss of the token price in the last 30 days | integer |
| liquidity\_usd | Liquidity of the token in USD | integer |
| liquidity\_wow | Change in liquidity week over week | integer |
| rolling\_one\_months\_trades | Number of trades in the last month | integer |
| transfers\_one\_month | Number of token transfers in the last month | integer |
| total\_volume\_week | Total trading volume of the token in the last 7 days | integer |
| total\_volume\_wow | Change in total trading volume week over week | integer |
| buy\_volume\_week | Total buying volume of the token in the last 7 days | integer |
| buy\_volume\_wow | Change in total buying volume week over week | integer |
| sell\_volume\_week | Total selling volume of the token in the last 7 days | integer |
| sell\_volume\_wow | Change in total selling volume week over week | integer |

#### Headers

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/farcaster/endpoint/farcaster_memecoins#parameter-x-dune-api-key)

X-Dune-Api-Key

string

required

API Key for the service

#### Query Parameters

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/farcaster/endpoint/farcaster_memecoins#parameter-api-key)

api\_key

string

API Key, alternative to using the HTTP header X-Dune-Api-Key

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/farcaster/endpoint/farcaster_memecoins#parameter-allow-partial-results)

allow\_partial\_results

boolean

This enables returning a query result that was too large and only a partial result is available. By default allow\_partial\_results is set to false and a failed state is returned.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/farcaster/endpoint/farcaster_memecoins#parameter-columns)

columns

string

Specifies a comma-separated list of column names to return. If omitted, all columns are included. Tip: use this to limit the result to specific columns, reducing datapoints cost of the call.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/farcaster/endpoint/farcaster_memecoins#parameter-filters)

filters

string

Expression to filter out rows from the results to return. This expression is similar to a SQL WHERE clause. More details about it in the Filtering section of the doc. This parameter is incompatible with sample\_count.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/farcaster/endpoint/farcaster_memecoins#parameter-ignore-max-datapoints-per-request)

ignore\_max\_datapoints\_per\_request

boolean

There is a default 250,000 datapoints limit to make sure you don't accidentally spend all your credits in one call. To ignore the max limit, you can add ignore\_max\_datapoints\_per\_request=true

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/farcaster/endpoint/farcaster_memecoins#parameter-limit)

limit

integer

Limit number of rows to return. This together with 'offset' allows easy pagination through results in an incremental and efficient way. This parameter is incompatible with sampling (sample\_count).

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/farcaster/endpoint/farcaster_memecoins#parameter-offset)

offset

integer

Offset row number to start (inclusive, first row means offset=0) returning results from. This together with 'limit' allows easy pagination through results in an incremental and efficient way. This parameter is incompatible with sampling (sample\_count).

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/farcaster/endpoint/farcaster_memecoins#parameter-query-id)

queryID

integer

required

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/farcaster/endpoint/farcaster_memecoins#parameter-sample-count)

sample\_count

integer

Number of rows to return from the result by sampling the data. This is useful when you want to get a uniform sample instead of the entire result. If the result has less than the sample count, the entire result is returned. Note that this will return a randomized sample, so not every call will return the same result. This parameter is incompatible with `offset`, `limit`, and `filters` parameters.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/farcaster/endpoint/farcaster_memecoins#parameter-sort-by)

sort\_by

string

Expression to define the order in which the results should be returned. This expression is similar to a SQL ORDER BY clause. More details about it in the Sorting section of the doc.

      "expires_at": "2024-12-20T11:04:18.724658237Z",

      "next_offset": 100,

        "metadata": {

      --header 'X-Dune-Api-Key: <x-dune-api-key>'

*   Query can be found [here](https://dune.com/queries/3633434)
    
*   Scheduled to update every 30 minutes
*   You can apply [filters](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/executions/filtering)
     like WHERE, IN, AND/OR upon results
*   Learn about channel tiers [in this article](https://read.cryptodatabytes.com/p/how-to-find-and-analyze-trends-on)
    

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/farcaster/endpoint/farcaster_channels#use-cases)

Use Cases
=====================================================================================================

*   Recommend trending channels based on engagement, casters, and/or domains
*   Curate feeds that segment channels by type (small and growing, large and established, influencer led)
*   Filter out likely bot channels (low engagement, no influencers or vips, no “onchain\_experts”)

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/farcaster/endpoint/farcaster_channels#column-descriptions)

Column Descriptions
=========================================================================================================================

| Column | Description | Type |
| --- | --- | --- |
| channel\_tier\_name | name of channel tier this week | string |
| channel\_tier | farcaster channel tier this week | integer |
| channel\_tier\_last | farcaster channel tier last week | integer |
| channel | farcaster channel name | string |
| channel\_age | age of channel in days | integer |
| influential\_casters | top casters by engagement in channel | array(string) |
| top\_domains | top domains in casts in channel | array(string) |
| top\_casters | top casters by number of casts in channel | array(string) |
| casters | number of casters in channels in the last week | integer |
| wow\_casters | week over week change in number of casters | integer |
| got\_casts | number of casts in channels in the last week | integer |
| wow\_cast | week over week change in number of casts | integer |
| engagement | engagement on channel casts in the last week | integer |
| wow\_engage | week over week change in number of engagement | integer |
| onchain\_experts | number of casters in the last week who have transacted 100+ times ever | integer |
| trading\_experts | number of casters in the last week who have traded $10k+ in DEX or NFT volume ever | integer |
| contract\_experts | number of casters in the last week who have deployed 10+ contracts ever | integer |
| active\_npc | npc tier users that have casted in the channel | integer |
| wow\_npc | week over week change in number of npc tier casters | integer |
| active\_user | active tier users that have casted in the channel | integer |
| wow\_active\_user | week over week change in number of active tier casters | integer |
| active\_star | star tier users that have casted in the channel | integer |
| wow\_star | week over week change in number of star tier casters | integer |
| active\_influencer | influencer tier users that have casted in the channel | integer |
| wow\_influencer | week over week change in number of influencer tier casters | integer |
| active\_vip | vip tier users that have casted in the channel | integer |
| wow\_vip | week over week change in number of vip tier casters | integer |
| got\_replies | number of replies in the last week | integer |
| wow\_reply | week over week change in number of replies | integer |
| got\_likes | number of likes in the last week | integer |
| wow\_likes | week over week change in number of likes | integer |
| got\_recasts | number of recasts in the last week | integer |
| wow\_recasts | week over week change in number of recasts | integer |

#### Headers

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/farcaster/endpoint/farcaster_channels#parameter-x-dune-api-key)

X-Dune-Api-Key

string

required

API Key for the service

#### Query Parameters

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/farcaster/endpoint/farcaster_channels#parameter-api-key)

api\_key

string

API Key, alternative to using the HTTP header X-Dune-Api-Key

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/farcaster/endpoint/farcaster_channels#parameter-allow-partial-results)

allow\_partial\_results

boolean

This enables returning a query result that was too large and only a partial result is available. By default allow\_partial\_results is set to false and a failed state is returned.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/farcaster/endpoint/farcaster_channels#parameter-columns)

columns

string

Specifies a comma-separated list of column names to return. If omitted, all columns are included. Tip: use this to limit the result to specific columns, reducing datapoints cost of the call.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/farcaster/endpoint/farcaster_channels#parameter-filters)

filters

string

Expression to filter out rows from the results to return. This expression is similar to a SQL WHERE clause. More details about it in the Filtering section of the doc. This parameter is incompatible with sample\_count.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/farcaster/endpoint/farcaster_channels#parameter-ignore-max-datapoints-per-request)

ignore\_max\_datapoints\_per\_request

boolean

There is a default 250,000 datapoints limit to make sure you don't accidentally spend all your credits in one call. To ignore the max limit, you can add ignore\_max\_datapoints\_per\_request=true

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/farcaster/endpoint/farcaster_channels#parameter-limit)

limit

integer

Limit number of rows to return. This together with 'offset' allows easy pagination through results in an incremental and efficient way. This parameter is incompatible with sampling (sample\_count).

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/farcaster/endpoint/farcaster_channels#parameter-offset)

offset

integer

Offset row number to start (inclusive, first row means offset=0) returning results from. This together with 'limit' allows easy pagination through results in an incremental and efficient way. This parameter is incompatible with sampling (sample\_count).

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/farcaster/endpoint/farcaster_channels#parameter-query-id)

queryID

integer

required

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/farcaster/endpoint/farcaster_channels#parameter-sample-count)

sample\_count

integer

Number of rows to return from the result by sampling the data. This is useful when you want to get a uniform sample instead of the entire result. If the result has less than the sample count, the entire result is returned. Note that this will return a randomized sample, so not every call will return the same result. This parameter is incompatible with `offset`, `limit`, and `filters` parameters.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/farcaster/endpoint/farcaster_channels#parameter-sort-by)

sort\_by

string

Expression to define the order in which the results should be returned. This expression is similar to a SQL ORDER BY clause. More details about it in the Sorting section of the doc.

#### Response

200

application/json

OK

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/farcaster/endpoint/farcaster_channels#response-cancelled-at)

cancelled\_at

string

Timestamp of when the query execution was cancelled, if applicable.

Example:

`"2024-12-20T11:04:18.724658237Z"`

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/farcaster/endpoint/farcaster_channels#response-error)

error

object

In case the execution had an error, this object will contain the error details

Show child attributes

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/farcaster/endpoint/farcaster_channels#response-execution-ended-at)

execution\_ended\_at

string

Timestamp of when the query execution ended.

Example:

`"2024-12-20T11:04:18.724658237Z"`

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/farcaster/endpoint/farcaster_channels#response-execution-id)

execution\_id

string

Unique identifier for the execution of the query.

Example:

`"01HKZJ2683PHF9Q9PHHQ8FW4Q1"`

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/farcaster/endpoint/farcaster_channels#response-execution-started-at)

execution\_started\_at

string

Timestamp of when the query execution started.

Example:

`"2024-12-20T11:04:18.724658237Z"`

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/farcaster/endpoint/farcaster_channels#response-expires-at)

expires\_at

string

Timestamp of when the query result expires.

Example:

`"2024-12-20T11:04:18.724658237Z"`

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/farcaster/endpoint/farcaster_channels#response-is-execution-finished)

is\_execution\_finished

boolean

Whether the state of the query execution is terminal. This can be used for polling purposes.

Example:

`true`

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/farcaster/endpoint/farcaster_channels#response-next-offset)

next\_offset

integer

Offset that can be used to retrieve the next page of results.

Example:

`100`

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/farcaster/endpoint/farcaster_channels#response-next-uri)

next\_uri

string

URI that can be used to fetch the next page of results.

Example:

`"https://api.dune.com/api/v1/execution/01HKZJ2683PHF9Q9PHHQ8FW4Q1/results?offset=100&limit=100"`

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/farcaster/endpoint/farcaster_channels#response-query-id)

query\_id

integer

Unique identifier of the query.

Example:

`1234`

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/farcaster/endpoint/farcaster_channels#response-result)

result

object

The object containing the results and metadata of the query execution

Show child attributes

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/farcaster/endpoint/farcaster_channels#response-state)

state

string

The state of the query execution.

Example:

`"QUERY_STATE_COMPLETED"`

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/farcaster/endpoint/farcaster_channels#response-submitted-at)

submitted\_at

string

Timestamp of when the query was submitted.

Example:

`"2024-12-20T11:04:18.724658237Z"`

GET

/

v1

/

execution

/

{execution\_id}

results

Try it

cURL

Python SDK

Python

Javascript

Go

PHP

Java

Copy

Ask AI

curl -X GET "https://api.dune.com/api/v1/execution/{{execution_id}}/results/csv" -H x-dune-api-key:{{api_key}}

200

400

401

404

500

Copy

Ask AI

    "<string>"

You must pass the `execution_id` obtained from making an [execute query](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/executions/endpoint/execute-query)
 POST request. Result returns the status, metadata, and query results (in CSV) from a query execution.

*   Read more on [Filtering](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/executions/filtering)
    , [Sorting](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/executions/sorting)
    , and [Sampling](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/executions/sampling)
     to learn more about flexibly grabbing query results.
*   Read more on [Pagination](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/executions/pagination)
     to get the most out of the API and handle large results.

*   Results data from an execution are stored with an expiration date of 90 days. This is visible on the API response on the “expires\_at” field in the execution status and results json body (not on the CSV endpoint).
*   Dune internally has a maximum query result size limit (which currently is 8GB, but subject to increase in the future). If your query yields more than 8GB of data, the result will be truncated in storage. In such cases, pulling the result data (using pagination) but without specifying `allow_partial_results` set to true will trigger an error message: “error”: “Partial Result, please request with ‘allows\_partial\_results=true’”. If you wish to retrieve partial results, you can pass the parameter `allow_partial_results=true`. But please make sure you indeed want to fetch the truncated result.

Execute query and get result in one call

If you are using the [Python SDK](https://github.com/duneanalytics/dune-client/tree/d2195b2a9577e2dcae5d2600cb3eddce20987f38)
, you can directly execute and fetch result in one function call, like below:

Python SDK

Copy

Ask AI

    
    import json
    from dune_client.types import QueryParameter
    from dune_client.client import DuneClient
    from dune_client.query import QueryBase
    
    # setup Dune Python client
    dune = DuneClient()
    
    

Use `run_query` to get result in JSON, `run_query_csv` to get result in CSV format, and `run_query_dataframe` to get result in Pandas dataframe

Copy

Ask AI

    
    result = dune.run_query(
        query=query # pass in query to run 
        , performance = 'large' # optionally define which tier to run the execution on (default is "medium")
        )

cURL

Python SDK

Python

Javascript

Go

PHP

Java

Copy

Ask AI

    
    curl -X GET "https://api.dune.com/api/v1/execution/{{execution_id}}/results/csv" -H x-dune-api-key:{{api_key}}
    
    

#### Headers

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/executions/endpoint/get-execution-result-csv#parameter-x-dune-api-key)

X-Dune-Api-Key

string

required

API Key for the service

#### Path Parameters

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/executions/endpoint/get-execution-result-csv#parameter-execution-id)

execution\_id

string

required

Execution ID

#### Query Parameters

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/executions/endpoint/get-execution-result-csv#parameter-api-key)

api\_key

string

Alternative to using the X-Dune-Api-Key header

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/executions/endpoint/get-execution-result-csv#parameter-allow-partial-results)

allow\_partial\_results

boolean

This enables returning a query result that was too large and only a partial result is available. By default allow\_partial\_results is set to false and a failed state is returned.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/executions/endpoint/get-execution-result-csv#parameter-columns)

columns

string

Specifies a comma-separated list of column names to return. If omitted, all columns are included. Tip: use this to limit the result to specific columns, reducing datapoints cost of the call.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/executions/endpoint/get-execution-result-csv#parameter-execution-id)

execution\_id

string

required

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/executions/endpoint/get-execution-result-csv#parameter-filters)

filters

string

Expression to filter out rows from the results to return. This expression is similar to a SQL WHERE clause. More details about it in the Filtering section of the doc. This parameter is incompatible with sample\_count.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/executions/endpoint/get-execution-result-csv#parameter-ignore-max-datapoints-per-request)

ignore\_max\_datapoints\_per\_request

boolean

There is a default 250,000 datapoints limit to make sure you don't accidentally spend all your credits in one call. To ignore the max limit, you can add ignore\_max\_datapoints\_per\_request=true

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/executions/endpoint/get-execution-result-csv#parameter-limit)

limit

integer

Limit number of rows to return. This together with 'offset' allows easy pagination through results in an incremental and efficient way. This parameter is incompatible with sampling (sample\_count).

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/executions/endpoint/get-execution-result-csv#parameter-offset)

offset

integer

Offset row number to start (inclusive, first row means offset=0) returning results from. This together with 'limit' allows easy pagination through results in an incremental and efficient way. This parameter is incompatible with sampling (sample\_count).

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/executions/endpoint/get-execution-result-csv#parameter-sample-count)

sample\_count

integer

Number of rows to return from the result by sampling the data. This is useful when you want to get a uniform sample instead of the entire result. If the result has less than the sample count, the entire result is returned. Note that this will return a randomized sample, so not every call will return the same result. This parameter is incompatible with `offset`, `limit`, and `filters` parameters.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/executions/endpoint/get-execution-result-csv#parameter-sort-by)

sort\_by

string

Expression to define the order in which the results should be returned. This expression is similar to a SQL ORDER BY clause. More details about it in the Sorting section of the doc.

#### Response

200

text/plain

OK

The response is of type `string`.

        "type": "syntax_error"
      },
      "execution_ended_at": "2024-12-20T11:04:18.724658237Z",
      "execution_id": "01HKZJ2683PHF9Q9PHHQ8FW4Q1",
      "execution_started_at": "2024-12-20T11:04:18.724658237Z",
      "expires_at": "2024-12-20T11:04:18.724658237Z",
      "is_execution_finished": true,
      "next_offset": 100,
      "next_uri": "https://api.dune.com/api/v1/execution/01HKZJ2683PHF9Q9PHHQ8FW4Q1/results?offset=100&limit=100",
      "query_id": 1234,
      "result": {
        "metadata": {
          "column_names": [\
            "Rank",\
            "Project",\
            "Volume"\
          ],
          "column_types": [\
            "double",\
            "varchar",\
            "bigint"\
          ],
          "datapoint_count": 1000,
          "execution_time_millis": 1000,
          "pending_time_millis": 1000,
          "result_set_bytes": 1000,
          "row_count": 10,
          "total_result_set_bytes": 10000,
          "total_row_count": 1000
        },
        "rows": [\
          {}\
        ],
        "update_type": "<string>"
      },
      "state": "QUERY_STATE_COMPLETED",
      "submitted_at": "2024-12-20T11:04:18.724658237Z"
    }

*   Query can be found [here](https://dune.com/queries/3633428)
    
*   Scheduled to update every 30 minutes
*   You can apply [filters](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/executions/filtering)
     like WHERE, IN, AND/OR upon results
*   Learn about user tiers [in this article](https://read.cryptodatabytes.com/p/how-to-find-and-analyze-trends-on)
    

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/farcaster/endpoint/farcaster_users#use-cases)

Use Cases
==================================================================================================

*   Recommend trending users based on engagement, domains, or onchain activity
*   Curate feeds that segment users by type (developer, artist, memecoin trader, etc.)
*   Filter out likely bot users (high number of casts, low engagement, low onchain activity)

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/farcaster/endpoint/farcaster_users#column-descriptions)

Column Descriptions
======================================================================================================================

| Column | Description | Type |
| --- | --- | --- |
| fid\_active\_tier\_name | name of Farcaster tier this week | string |
| fid\_active\_tier | Farcaster user tier this week | integer |
| fid\_active\_tier\_last | Farcaster user tier last week | integer |
| fid | Farcaster user id | integer |
| fname | Farcaster username of user | string |
| account\_age | age of account in days | integer |
| channels | number of channels cast in during the last week | integer |
| top\_channels | top channels cast in | array(string) |
| top\_domains | top domains cast | array(string) |
| top\_engagers | top cast engagers | array(string) |
| followers | total number of followers | integer |
| wow\_followers | week over week change in number of followers | integer |
| casts | number of casts in the last week | integer |
| wow\_casts | week over week change in number of casts | integer |
| engagement | engagement on user casts in the last week | integer |
| wow\_engage | week over week change in number of engagements | integer |
| total\_transactions | total number of wallet transactions | integer |
| trading\_volume\_usd | total NFT and DEX trading volume (USD) | integer |
| contracts\_deployed | total number of deployed contracts | integer |
| got\_likes | number of likes in the last week | integer |
| wow\_likes | week over week change in number of likes | integer |
| got\_recasts | number of recasts in the last week | integer |
| wow\_recasts | week over week change in number of recasts | integer |
| got\_replies | number of replies in the last week | integer |
| wow\_replies | week over week change in number of replies | integer |
| addresses | user verified addresses | array(string) |

#### Headers

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/farcaster/endpoint/farcaster_users#parameter-x-dune-api-key)

X-Dune-Api-Key

string

required

API Key for the service

#### Query Parameters

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/farcaster/endpoint/farcaster_users#parameter-api-key)

api\_key

string

API Key, alternative to using the HTTP header X-Dune-Api-Key

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/farcaster/endpoint/farcaster_users#parameter-allow-partial-results)

allow\_partial\_results

boolean

This enables returning a query result that was too large and only a partial result is available. By default allow\_partial\_results is set to false and a failed state is returned.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/farcaster/endpoint/farcaster_users#parameter-columns)

columns

string

Specifies a comma-separated list of column names to return. If omitted, all columns are included. Tip: use this to limit the result to specific columns, reducing datapoints cost of the call.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/farcaster/endpoint/farcaster_users#parameter-filters)

filters

string

Expression to filter out rows from the results to return. This expression is similar to a SQL WHERE clause. More details about it in the Filtering section of the doc. This parameter is incompatible with sample\_count.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/farcaster/endpoint/farcaster_users#parameter-ignore-max-datapoints-per-request)

ignore\_max\_datapoints\_per\_request

boolean

There is a default 250,000 datapoints limit to make sure you don't accidentally spend all your credits in one call. To ignore the max limit, you can add ignore\_max\_datapoints\_per\_request=true

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/farcaster/endpoint/farcaster_users#parameter-limit)

limit

integer

Limit number of rows to return. This together with 'offset' allows easy pagination through results in an incremental and efficient way. This parameter is incompatible with sampling (sample\_count).

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/farcaster/endpoint/farcaster_users#parameter-offset)

offset

integer

Offset row number to start (inclusive, first row means offset=0) returning results from. This together with 'limit' allows easy pagination through results in an incremental and efficient way. This parameter is incompatible with sampling (sample\_count).

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/farcaster/endpoint/farcaster_users#parameter-query-id)

queryID

integer

required

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/farcaster/endpoint/farcaster_users#parameter-sample-count)

sample\_count

integer

Number of rows to return from the result by sampling the data. This is useful when you want to get a uniform sample instead of the entire result. If the result has less than the sample count, the entire result is returned. Note that this will return a randomized sample, so not every call will return the same result. This parameter is incompatible with `offset`, `limit`, and `filters` parameters.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/farcaster/endpoint/farcaster_users#parameter-sort-by)

sort\_by

string

Expression to define the order in which the results should be returned. This expression is similar to a SQL ORDER BY clause. More details about it in the Sorting section of the doc.

#### Response

200

application/json

OK

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/farcaster/endpoint/farcaster_users#response-cancelled-at)

cancelled\_at

string

Timestamp of when the query execution was cancelled, if applicable.

Example:

`"2024-12-20T11:04:18.724658237Z"`

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/farcaster/endpoint/farcaster_users#response-error)

error

object

In case the execution had an error, this object will contain the error details

Show child attributes

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/farcaster/endpoint/farcaster_users#response-execution-ended-at)

execution\_ended\_at

string

Timestamp of when the query execution ended.

Example:

`"2024-12-20T11:04:18.724658237Z"`

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/farcaster/endpoint/farcaster_users#response-execution-id)

execution\_id

string

Unique identifier for the execution of the query.

Example:

`"01HKZJ2683PHF9Q9PHHQ8FW4Q1"`

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/farcaster/endpoint/farcaster_users#response-execution-started-at)

execution\_started\_at

string

Timestamp of when the query execution started.

Example:

`"2024-12-20T11:04:18.724658237Z"`

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/farcaster/endpoint/farcaster_users#response-expires-at)

expires\_at

string

Timestamp of when the query result expires.

Example:

`"2024-12-20T11:04:18.724658237Z"`

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/farcaster/endpoint/farcaster_users#response-is-execution-finished)

is\_execution\_finished

boolean

Whether the state of the query execution is terminal. This can be used for polling purposes.

Example:

`true`

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/farcaster/endpoint/farcaster_users#response-next-offset)

next\_offset

integer

Offset that can be used to retrieve the next page of results.

Example:

`100`

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/farcaster/endpoint/farcaster_users#response-next-uri)

next\_uri

string

URI that can be used to fetch the next page of results.

Example:

`"https://api.dune.com/api/v1/execution/01HKZJ2683PHF9Q9PHHQ8FW4Q1/results?offset=100&limit=100"`

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/farcaster/endpoint/farcaster_users#response-query-id)

query\_id

integer

Unique identifier of the query.

Example:

`1234`

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/farcaster/endpoint/farcaster_users#response-result)

result

object

The object containing the results and metadata of the query execution

Show child attributes

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/farcaster/endpoint/farcaster_users#response-state)

state

string

The state of the query execution.

Example:

`"QUERY_STATE_COMPLETED"`

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/farcaster/endpoint/farcaster_users#response-submitted-at)

submitted\_at

string

Timestamp of when the query was submitted.

Example:

`"2024-12-20T11:04:18.724658237Z"`

      "execution_started_at": "2024-12-20T11:04:18.724658237Z",

      "is_execution_finished": true,
      "next_offset": 100,
      "next_uri": "https://api.dune.com/api/v1/execution/01HKZJ2683PHF9Q9PHHQ8FW4Q1/results?offset=100&limit=100",

            "bigint"\

          "execution_time_millis": 1000,
          "pending_time_millis": 1000,
          "result_set_bytes": 1000,
          "row_count": 10,
          "total_result_set_bytes": 10000,
          "total_row_count": 1000
        },
        "rows": [\
          {}\
        ],
        "update_type": "<string>"
      },
      "state": "QUERY_STATE_COMPLETED",
      "submitted_at": "2024-12-20T11:04:18.724658237Z"
    }

You must pass the `execution_id` obtained from making an [execute query](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/executions/endpoint/execute-query)
 POST request. Result returns the status, metadata, and query results (in JSON) from a query execution.

*   Read more on [Filtering](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/executions/filtering)
    , [Sorting](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/executions/sorting)
    , and [Sampling](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/executions/sampling)
     to learn more about flexibly grabbing query results.
*   Read more on [Pagination](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/executions/pagination)
     to get the most out of the API and handle large results.

*   Results data from an execution are stored for 90 days. This is visible on the API response on the “expires\_at” field in the execution status and results body.
*   Dune internally has a maximum query result size limit (which currently is 8GB, but subject to increase in the future). If your query yields more than 8GB of data, the result will be truncated in storage. In such cases, pulling the result data (using pagination) but without specifying `allow_partial_results` set to true will trigger an error message: “error”: “Partial Result, please request with ‘allows\_partial\_results=true’”. If you wish to retrieve partial results, you can pass the parameter `allow_partial_results=true`. But please make sure you indeed want to fetch the truncated result.

Execute query and get result in one call

If you are using the [Python SDK](https://github.com/duneanalytics/dune-client/tree/d2195b2a9577e2dcae5d2600cb3eddce20987f38)
 or community [Typescript SDK](https://github.com/bh2smith/ts-dune-client)
, you can directly execute and fetch a result in one function call, like below:

*   Python SDK
    
*   Typescript SDK
    

Copy

Ask AI

    
    import json
    from dune_client.types import QueryParameter
    from dune_client.client import DuneClient
    from dune_client.query import QueryBase
    
    # setup Dune Python client
    dune = DuneClient()
    
    

Use `run_query` to get result in JSON, `run_query_csv` to get result in CSV format, and `run_query_dataframe` to get result in Pandas dataframe

Copy

Ask AI

    
    result = dune.run_query(
        query=query # pass in query to run 
        , performance = 'large' # optionally define which tier to run the execution on (default is "medium")
        )

string

boolean

This enables returning a query result that was too large and only a partial result is available. By default allow\_partial\_results is set to false and a failed state is returned.

string

Specifies a comma-separated list of column names to return. If omitted, all columns are included. Tip: use this to limit the result to specific columns, reducing datapoints cost of the call.

integer

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/executions/endpoint/get-execution-result#parameter-sample-count)

integer

If the result has less than the sample count, the entire result is returned. Note that this will return a randomized sample, so not every call will return the same result. Materialized Views

Delete Materialized View

This deletes a materialized view given a full name

cURL

Copy

Ask AI

    curl --request DELETE \
      --url https://api.dune.com/api/v1/materialized-views/{name} \
      --header 'X-Dune-Api-Key: <x-dune-api-key>'

200

400

401

403

404

500

Copy

Ask AI

    {
      "message": "<string>"
    }

DELETE

/

v1

/

materialized-views

/

{name}

Try it

This deletes a materialized view given a full name

cURL

Copy

Ask AI

    curl --request DELETE \
      --url https://api.dune.com/api/v1/materialized-views/{name} \
      --header 'X-Dune-Api-Key: <x-dune-api-key>'

200

400

401

403

404

500

Copy

Ask AI

    {
      "message": "<string>"
    }

*   The name must be the full name qualifier for the materialized view, i.e. `dune.<your_team>.<name>`

#### Headers

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/materialized-views/delete#parameter-x-dune-api-key)

X-Dune-Api-Key

string

required

API Key for the service

#### Path Parameters

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/materialized-views/delete#parameter-name)

name

string

required

Matview Name

#### Query Parameters

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/materialized-views/delete#parameter-api-key)

api\_key

string

API Key, alternative to using the HTTP header X-Dune-Api-Key

#### Response

200

application/json

OK

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/materialized-views/delete#response-message)

message

string

      "submitted_at": "2024-12-20T11:04:18.724658237Z"
    }

You must pass parameter query\_id. Returns the latest execution id and results (in JSON) of that latest run, regardless of the job id/run or if it is run in the app or the api. The query specified must either be public or a query you have ownership of (you or a team you belong to have ownership).

*   This endpoint does NOT trigger an execution but does [consume credits through datapoints](https://dune.com/pricing)
    .
*   Read more on [Filtering](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/executions/filtering)
    , [Sorting](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/executions/sorting)
    , and [Sampling](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/executions/sampling)
     to learn more about flexibly grabbing query results.
*   Read more on [Pagination](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/executions/pagination)
     to get the most out of the API and handle large results.

*   Dune internally has a maximum query result size limit (which currently is 8GB, but subject to increase in the future). If your query yields more than 8GB of data, the result will be truncated in storage. In such cases, pulling the result data (using pagination) but without specifying `allow_partial_results` set to true will trigger an error message: “error”: “Partial Result, please request with ‘allows\_partial\_results=true’”. If you wish to retrieve partial results, you can pass the parameter `allow_partial_results=true`. But please make sure you indeed want to fetch the truncated result.

Execute query and get result in one call

If you are using the [Python SDK](https://github.com/duneanalytics/dune-client/tree/d2195b2a9577e2dcae5d2600cb3eddce20987f38)
, you can directly execute and fetch result in one function call, like below:

Python SDK

Copy

Ask AI

    
    import json
    from dune_client.types import QueryParameter
    from dune_client.client import DuneClient
    from dune_client.query import QueryBase
    
    # setup Dune Python client
    dune = DuneClient()
    
    

Use `run_query` to get result in JSON, `run_query_csv` to get result in CSV format, and `run_query_dataframe` to get result in Pandas dataframe

Copy

Ask AI

    
    result = dune.run_query(
        query=query # pass in query to run 
        , performance = 'large' # optionally define which tier to run the execution on (default is "medium")
        )

cURL

Python SDK

Python

Javascript

Go

PHP

Java

Copy

Ask AI

    
    curl --request GET \
      --url https://api.dune.com/api/v1/query/{query_id}/results
      
    

#### Headers

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/executions/endpoint/get-query-result#parameter-x-dune-api-key)

X-Dune-Api-Key

string

required

API Key for the service

#### Path Parameters

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/executions/endpoint/get-query-result#parameter-query-id)

query\_id

string

required

Query ID

#### Query Parameters

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/executions/endpoint/get-query-result#parameter-api-key)

api\_key

string

Alternative to using the X-Dune-Api-Key header

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/executions/endpoint/get-query-result#parameter-allow-partial-results)

allow\_partial\_results

boolean

This enables returning a query result that was too large and only a partial result is available. By default allow\_partial\_results is set to false and a failed state is returned.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/executions/endpoint/get-query-result#parameter-columns)

columns

string

Specifies a comma-separated list of column names to return. If omitted, all columns are included. Tip: use this to limit the result to specific columns, reducing datapoints cost of the call.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/executions/endpoint/get-query-result#parameter-filters)

filters

string

Expression to filter out rows from the results to return. This expression is similar to a SQL WHERE clause. More details about it in the Filtering section of the doc. This parameter is incompatible with sample\_count.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/executions/endpoint/get-query-result#parameter-ignore-max-datapoints-per-request)

ignore\_max\_datapoints\_per\_request

boolean

There is a default 250,000 datapoints limit to make sure you don't accidentally spend all your credits in one call. To ignore the max limit, you can add ignore\_max\_datapoints\_per\_request=true

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/executions/endpoint/get-query-result#parameter-limit)

limit

integer

Limit number of rows to return. This together with 'offset' allows easy pagination through results in an incremental and efficient way. This parameter is incompatible with sampling (sample\_count).

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/executions/endpoint/get-query-result#parameter-offset)

offset

integer

Offset row number to start (inclusive, first row means offset=0) returning results from. This together with 'limit' allows easy pagination through results in an incremental and efficient way. This parameter is incompatible with sampling (sample\_count).

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/executions/endpoint/get-query-result#parameter-query-id)

queryID

integer

required

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/executions/endpoint/get-query-result#parameter-sample-count)

sample\_count

integer

Number of rows to return from the result by sampling the data. This is useful when you want to get a uniform sample instead of the entire result. If the result has less than the sample count, the entire result is returned. Note that this will return a randomized sample, so not every call will return the same result. This parameter is incompatible with `offset`, `limit`, and `filters` parameters.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/executions/endpoint/get-query-result#parameter-sort-by)

sort\_by

string

Expression to define the order in which the results should be returned. This expression is similar to a SQL ORDER BY clause. More details about it in the Sorting section of the doc.

#### Response

200

application/json

OK

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/executions/endpoint/get-query-result#response-cancelled-at)

cancelled\_at

string

Timestamp of when the query execution was cancelled, if applicable.

Example:

`"2024-12-20T11:04:18.724658237Z"`

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/executions/endpoint/get-query-result#response-error)

error

object

In case the execution had an error, this object will contain the error details

Show child attributes

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/executions/endpoint/get-query-result#response-execution-ended-at)

execution\_ended\_at

string

Timestamp of when the query execution ended.

Example:

`"2024-12-20T11:04:18.724658237Z"`

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/executions/endpoint/get-query-result#response-execution-id)

execution\_id

string

Unique identifier for the execution of the query.

Example:

`"01HKZJ2683PHF9Q9PHHQ8FW4Q1"`

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/executions/endpoint/get-query-result#response-execution-started-at)

execution\_started\_at

string

Timestamp of when the query execution started.

Example:

`"2024-12-20T11:04:18.724658237Z"`

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/executions/endpoint/get-query-result#response-expires-at)

expires\_at

string

Timestamp of when the query result expires.

Example:

`"2024-12-20T11:04:18.724658237Z"`

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/executions/endpoint/get-query-result#response-is-execution-finished)

is\_execution\_finished

boolean

Whether the state of the query execution is terminal. This can be used for polling purposes.

Example:

`true`

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/executions/endpoint/get-query-result#response-next-offset)

next\_offset

integer

Offset that can be used to retrieve the next page of results.

Example:

`100`

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/executions/endpoint/get-query-result#response-next-uri)

next\_uri

string

URI that can be used to fetch the next page of results.

Example:

`"https://api.dune.com/api/v1/execution/01HKZJ2683PHF9Q9PHHQ8FW4Q1/results?offset=100&limit=100"`

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/executions/endpoint/get-query-result#response-query-id)

query\_id

integer

Unique identifier of the query.

Example:

`1234`

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/executions/endpoint/get-query-result#response-result)

result

object

The object containing the results and metadata of the query execution

Show child attributes

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/executions/endpoint/get-query-result#response-state)

state

string

The state of the query execution.

Example:

`"QUERY_STATE_COMPLETED"`

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/executions/endpoint/get-query-result#response-submitted-at)

submitted\_at

string

Timestamp of when the query was submitted.

Example:

`"2024-12-20T11:04:18.724658237Z"`

# Get Execution Status - Dune Docs

[Skip to main content](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/executions/endpoint/get-execution-status#content-area)

      "execution_id": "01HKZJ2683PHF9Q9PHHQ8FW4Q1",
      "query_id": 3493826,
      "is_execution_finished": true,
      "state": "QUERY_STATE_COMPLETED",
      "submitted_at": "2025-10-22T10:31:04.222464Z",
      "expires_at": "2026-01-20T10:31:04.36241Z",
      "execution_started_at": "2025-10-22T10:31:05.123456Z",

GET

/

v1

/

execution

/

{execution\_id}

/

status

Try it

cURL

Python SDK

Python

Javascript

Go

PHP

Java

Copy

Ask AI

curl -X GET "https://api.dune.com/api/v1/execution/{{execution_id}}/status" -H x-dune-api-key:{{api_key}}

Success Response

Error Response

Copy

Ask AI

{
      "execution_id": "01HKZJ2683PHF9Q9PHHQ8FW4Q1",
      "query_id": 3493826,
      "is_execution_finished": true,
      "state": "QUERY_STATE_COMPLETED",
      "submitted_at": "2025-10-22T10:31:04.222464Z",
      "expires_at": "2026-01-20T10:31:04.36241Z",
      "execution_started_at": "2025-10-22T10:31:05.123456Z",
      "execution_ended_at": "2025-10-22T10:31:15.789012Z",
      "execution_cost_credits": 10
    }

You must pass the `execution_id` obtained from making an [execute query](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/executions/endpoint/execute-query)
 or [execute SQL](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/executions/endpoint/execute-sql)
 POST request. Returns the status of a query execution along with relevant metadata of the results if the execution is completed. **This endpoint now includes detailed error information when a query fails**, eliminating the need to call the results endpoint just to get error details.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/executions/endpoint/get-execution-status#pricing)

Pricing
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

This endpoint has **no charge** and does not consume credits.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/executions/endpoint/get-execution-status#execution-states)

Execution States
----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Once an execution is triggered, it can be in one of the following states:

*   `QUERY_STATE_PENDING`: The query execution is waiting for an execution slot.
*   `QUERY_STATE_EXECUTING`: The query is currently executing.
*   `QUERY_STATE_FAILED`: The query execution failed. This is a terminal state. **The response will include detailed error information.**
*   `QUERY_STATE_COMPLETED`: The query execution completed successfully. You can retrieve the query result for this execution\_id.
*   `QUERY_STATE_CANCELED`: The query execution was canceled by the user.
*   `QUERY_STATE_EXPIRED`: The query execution expired, and the result is no longer available.
*   `QUERY_STATE_COMPLETED_PARTIAL`: The query execution was successful, but the result was truncated because it was too large. To receive the truncated result, set the `allow_partial_results` flag to `true` in the API request to fetch the result.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/executions/endpoint/get-execution-status#error-response-fields)

Error Response Fields
--------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

When a query execution fails (`QUERY_STATE_FAILED`), the response includes an `error` object with the following fields:

*   **type** (string): Error type classification (e.g., `FAILED_TYPE_EXECUTION_FAILED`)
*   **message** (string): Detailed error message explaining what went wrong, including line and column information
*   **metadata** (object): Additional error context
    *   **line** (integer): Line number where the error occurred
    *   **column** (integer): Column position where the error occurred

      "state": "QUERY_STATE_COMPLETED",
      "submitted_at": "2025-10-22T10:31:04.222464Z",
      "expires_at": "2026-01-20T10:31:04.36241Z",
      "execution_started_at": "2025-10-22T10:31:05.123456Z",
      "execution_ended_at": "2025-10-22T10:31:15.789012Z",
      "execution_cost_credits": 10
    }

Timestamp of when the query execution ended.

Example:

`"2024-12-20T11:04:18.724658237Z"`

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/executions/endpoint/get-execution-status#response-execution-id)

execution\_id

string

Unique identifier for the execution of the query and corresponding result.

Example:

`"01HKZJ2683PHF9Q9PHHQ8FW4Q1"`

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/executions/endpoint/get-execution-status#response-execution-started-at)

execution\_started\_at

string

Timestamp of when the query execution started.

Example:

`"2024-12-20T11:04:18.724658237Z"`

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/executions/endpoint/get-execution-status#response-expires-at)

expires\_at

string

Timestamp of when the query result expires.

Example:

`"2024-12-20T11:04:18.724658237Z"`

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/executions/endpoint/get-execution-status#response-is-execution-finished)

is\_execution\_finished

boolean

Whether the state of the query execution is terminal. This can be used for polling purposes.

Example:

`true`

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/executions/endpoint/get-execution-status#response-max-inflight-interactive-executions)

max\_inflight\_interactive\_executions

integer

Number of interactive executions this customer can have running in parallel

Example:

`3`

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/executions/endpoint/get-execution-status#response-max-inflight-interactive-reached)

max\_inflight\_interactive\_reached

integer

Total number of interactive executions this user has submitted which are still in progress only set to > 0 if the user has reached the limit of concurrent interactive executions

Example:

`5`

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/executions/endpoint/get-execution-status#response-query-id)

query\_id

integer

Unique identifier of the query.

Example:

`1234`

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/executions/endpoint/get-execution-status#response-queue-position)

queue\_position

integer

Example:

object

Metadata about the execution of the query, including details like column names, row counts, and execution times.

# Get Latest Query Result in CSV - Dune Docs

[Dune Docs home page![light logo](https://mintcdn.com/dune/uyJ-jHeSRFvNrzyu/logo/dune-logo-light.png?fit=max&auto=format&n=uyJ-jHeSRFvNrzyu&q=85&s=fbdf0e7e6fabc31e49afcdb53cb5e774)![dark logo](https://mintcdn.com/dune/uyJ-jHeSRFvNrzyu/logo/dune-logo-dark.png?fit=max&auto=format&n=uyJ-jHeSRFvNrzyu&q=85&s=767370d661596e21a7b3a4525d50d77e)](https://dune.com/)

Ask AI

curl --request GET \
      --url https://api.dune.com/api/v1/query/{query_id}/results/csv

200

400

404

500

Copy

Ask AI

    "<string>"

You must pass parameter query\_id. Returns the latest execution id and results (in CSV) of that latest run, regardless of the job id/run or if it is run in the app or the api. The query specified must either be public or a query you have ownership of (you or a team you belong to have ownership).

*   This endpoint does NOT trigger an execution but does [consume credits through datapoints](https://dune.com/pricing)
    .
*   Read more on [Filtering](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/executions/filtering)
    , [Sorting](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/executions/sorting)
    , and [Sampling](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/executions/sampling)
     to learn more about flexibly grabbing query results.
*   Read more on [Pagination](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/executions/pagination)
     to get the most out of the API and handle large results.

*   Dune internally has a maximum query result size limit (which currently is 8GB, but subject to increase in the future). If your query yields more than 8GB of data, the result will be truncated in storage. In such cases, pulling the result data (using pagination) but without specifying `allow_partial_results` set to true will trigger an error message: “error”: “Partial Result, please request with ‘allows\_partial\_results=true’”. If you wish to retrieve partial results, you can pass the parameter `allow_partial_results=true`. But please make sure you indeed want to fetch the truncated result.

Execute query and get result in one call

If you are using the [Python SDK](https://github.com/duneanalytics/dune-client/tree/d2195b2a9577e2dcae5d2600cb3eddce20987f38)
, you can directly execute and fetch result in one function call, like below:

Python SDK

Copy

Ask AI

    
    import json
    from dune_client.types import QueryParameter
    from dune_client.client import DuneClient
    from dune_client.query import QueryBase
    
    # setup Dune Python client
    dune = DuneClient()
    
    

Use `run_query` to get result in JSON, `run_query_csv` to get result in CSV format, and `run_query_dataframe` to get result in Pandas dataframe.

Copy

Ask AI

    
    result = dune.run_query(
        query=query # pass in query to run 
        , performance = 'large' # optionally define which tier to run the execution on (default is "medium")
        )

cURL

Python SDK

Python

Javascript

Go

PHP

Java

Copy

Ask AI

    
    curl --request GET \
      --url https://api.dune.com/api/v1/query/{query_id}/results/csv
    
    

#### Headers

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/executions/endpoint/get-query-result-csv#parameter-x-dune-api-key)

X-Dune-Api-Key

string

required

API Key for the service

#### Path Parameters

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/executions/endpoint/get-query-result-csv#parameter-query-id)

query\_id

string

required

Query ID

#### Query Parameters

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/executions/endpoint/get-query-result-csv#parameter-api-key)

api\_key

string

Alternative to using the X-Dune-Api-Key header

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/executions/endpoint/get-query-result-csv#parameter-allow-partial-results)

allow\_partial\_results

boolean

This enables returning a query result that was too large and only a partial result is available. By default allow\_partial\_results is set to false and a failed state is returned.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/executions/endpoint/get-query-result-csv#parameter-columns)

columns

string

Specifies a comma-separated list of column names to return. If omitted, all columns are included. Tip: use this to limit the result to specific columns, reducing datapoints cost of the call.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/executions/endpoint/get-query-result-csv#parameter-filters)

filters

string

Expression to filter out rows from the results to return. This expression is similar to a SQL WHERE clause. More details about it in the Filtering section of the doc. This parameter is incompatible with sample\_count.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/executions/endpoint/get-query-result-csv#parameter-ignore-max-datapoints-per-request)

ignore\_max\_datapoints\_per\_request

boolean

There is a default 250,000 datapoints limit to make sure you don't accidentally spend all your credits in one call. To ignore the max limit, you can add ignore\_max\_datapoints\_per\_request=true

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/executions/endpoint/get-query-result-csv#parameter-limit)

limit

integer

Limit number of rows to return. This together with 'offset' allows easy pagination through results in an incremental and efficient way. This parameter is incompatible with sampling (sample\_count).

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/executions/endpoint/get-query-result-csv#parameter-offset)

offset

integer

Offset row number to start (inclusive, first row means offset=0) returning results from. This together with 'limit' allows easy pagination through results in an incremental and efficient way. This parameter is incompatible with sampling (sample\_count).

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/executions/endpoint/get-query-result-csv#parameter-query-id)

queryID

integer

required

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/executions/endpoint/get-query-result-csv#parameter-sample-count)

sample\_count

integer

Number of rows to return from the result by sampling the data. This is useful when you want to get a uniform sample instead of the entire result. If the result has less than the sample count, the entire result is returned. Note that this will return a randomized sample, so not every call will return the same result. This parameter is incompatible with `offset`, `limit`, and `filters` parameters.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/executions/endpoint/get-query-result-csv#parameter-sort-by)

sort\_by

string

Expression to define the order in which the results should be returned. This expression is similar to a SQL ORDER BY clause. More details about it in the Sorting section of the doc.

#### Response

200

text/plain

OK

The response is of type `string`.

# dex.trades on kaia - Dune Docs

[Skip to main content](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/evm/kaia/curated-data/dex/dex-trades#content-area)

[Dune Docs home page![light logo](https://mintcdn.com/dune/uyJ-jHeSRFvNrzyu/logo/dune-logo-light.png?fit=max&auto=format&n=uyJ-jHeSRFvNrzyu&q=85&s=fbdf0e7e6fabc31e49afcdb53cb5e774)![dark logo](https://mintcdn.com/dune/uyJ-jHeSRFvNrzyu/logo/dune-logo-dark.png?fit=max&auto=format&n=uyJ-jHeSRFvNrzyu&q=85&s=767370d661596e21a7b3a4525d50d77e)](https://dune.com/)

Search...

⌘K

Search...

Navigation

DEX

dex.trades on kaia

[Get Started](https://docs.dune.com/home)
[Analytics Studio](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/overview)
[Query Engine](https://docs.dune.com/query-engine/overview)
[Data Catalog](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/overview)
[Analytics API](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/overview/introduction)
[Datashare](https://docs.dune.com/datashare/datashare)
[Catalyst](https://docs.dune.com/catalyst/overview)

This is a cross-chain table but can be filtered for kaia transactions.

Table Description
-----------------

The `dex.trades` table captures detailed data on trades executed via decentralized exchanges (DEXs). This table captures all raw trade events that happen across all liqudity pools. It provides a comprehensive view of the entire trade execution process, detailing the specific paths and liquidity sources utilized.

Functional Overview
-------------------

The `dex.trades` table provides an in-depth view of trades on decentralized exchanges like Uniswap or Curve. This table includes entries for each segment of a trade that passes through different liquidity pools, as well as single-step trades. For example, a user may initiate a trade to swap USDC for PEPE. If this trade is executed through multiple liquidity pools, such as USDC-WETH and WETH-PEPE, the `dex.trades` table will record each segment of the trade as a separate entry. Conversely, a single-step trade, such as directly swapping USDC for ETH, will be recorded as a single entry.This detailed approach allows for granular analysis of trade execution paths, enabling users to:

*   **Analyze Liquidity Sources:** Understand which liquidity pools are used and how they interact in both single-step and multi-step trades.
*   **Track Trade Execution Paths:** Follow the exact route a trade takes across different DEXs and liquidity pools
*   **Assess Slippage and Execution Quality:** Evaluate the impact of each step on the overall trade execution, including slippage and price changes.
*   **Monitor Market Dynamics:** Gain insights into the behavior and dynamics of different liquidity pools and DEXs over time.

Table Coverage
--------------

The following table shows which projects and versions of those projects are covered in the `dex.trades` table on kaia.

Column Descriptions
-------------------

Datatypes on Snowflake datashare are different in some cases, read more [here](https://docs.dune.com/datashare/datashare#datatypes)
.

# NFT.trades on kaia - Dune Docs

[Skip to main content](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/evm/kaia/curated-data/nft/nft-trades#content-area)

[Dune Docs home page![light logo](https://mintcdn.com/dune/uyJ-jHeSRFvNrzyu/logo/dune-logo-light.png?fit=max&auto=format&n=uyJ-jHeSRFvNrzyu&q=85&s=fbdf0e7e6fabc31e49afcdb53cb5e774)![dark logo](https://mintcdn.com/dune/uyJ-jHeSRFvNrzyu/logo/dune-logo-dark.png?fit=max&auto=format&n=uyJ-jHeSRFvNrzyu&q=85&s=767370d661596e21a7b3a4525d50d77e)](https://dune.com/)

This is a cross-chain table but can be filtered for kaia transactions.

Table Description
-----------------

The \`nft.trades\` table on Dune Analytics is central to capturing and analyzing Non-Fungible Token (NFT) transactions across various marketplaces. It is a pivotal resource for dissecting the intricacies of NFT trade execution, market behavior, and collector activity within the NFT space.

Usage
-----

The \`nft.trades\` table serves as an essential tool for delving into the NFT market's complexities. It offers a detailed snapshot of each NFT transaction, encompassing data points such as sale price, transaction timestamp, buyer and seller addresses, and the specific NFT assets involved. This table allows analysts to explore trends in NFT valuation, trading volumes, and marketplace dynamics, providing insights into the evolving landscape of digital collectibles and art.
