# Executions - Dune Docs

[Skip to main content](https://docs.dune.com/query-engine/query-executions#content-area)

[Dune Docs home page![light logo](https://mintcdn.com/dune/uyJ-jHeSRFvNrzyu/logo/dune-logo-light.png?fit=max&auto=format&n=uyJ-jHeSRFvNrzyu&q=85&s=fbdf0e7e6fabc31e49afcdb53cb5e774)![dark logo](https://mintcdn.com/dune/uyJ-jHeSRFvNrzyu/logo/dune-logo-dark.png?fit=max&auto=format&n=uyJ-jHeSRFvNrzyu&q=85&s=767370d661596e21a7b3a4525d50d77e)](https://dune.com/)

Navigation

Functionality

Executions

[Get Started](https://docs.dune.com/home)
[Analytics Studio](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/overview)
[Query Engine](https://docs.dune.com/query-engine/overview)
[Data Catalog](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/overview)
[Analytics API](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/overview/introduction)
[Datashare](https://docs.dune.com/datashare/datashare)
[Catalyst](https://docs.dune.com/catalyst/overview)

On this page

*   [Overview](https://docs.dune.com/query-engine/query-executions#overview)
    
*   [Query executions triggers](https://docs.dune.com/query-engine/query-executions#query-executions-triggers)
    
*   [Query engine size](https://docs.dune.com/query-engine/query-executions#query-engine-size)
    
*   [Small engine size](https://docs.dune.com/query-engine/query-executions#small-engine-size)
    
*   [Medium engine size](https://docs.dune.com/query-engine/query-executions#medium-engine-size)
    
*   [Large engine size](https://docs.dune.com/query-engine/query-executions#large-engine-size)
    

[​](https://docs.dune.com/query-engine/query-executions#overview)

Overview
=============================================================================

**Queries on Dune need to be triggered and will be executed on one of our query engines.** Query executions can be triggered by any user/team in Dune for public queries and by the owner of the query for private queries. Query executions can be triggered through the query editor, the dashboard editor, or via the API. We also automatically refresh popular dashboards automatically in regular intervals. The query engine determines the amount of resources allocated to your query. The larger the query engine, the more resources are allocated to your query. This means that queries executed on a larger query engine will run faster and are less likely to time out.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/query-engine/query-executions#query-executions-triggers)

Query executions triggers
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Query executions on Dune are triggered in four ways:

1.  **Interactive executions** are manually triggered by a user clicking the “Run” button in the query editor page or refreshing an entire dashboard. Interactive executions can be routed via the small, medium, or large cluster, depending on the query engine selected.
2.  **Scheduled executions** are triggered at a specific time and frequency. Scheduled executions can be routed via the medium or large cluster, depending on the execution tier selected.
3.  **API executions** are triggered by an API call. API executions can be routed via the small, medium, or large cluster, depending on the query engine selected.
4.  **Popular dashboards** are automatically refreshed based on their popularity. We measure popularity based on the number of views a dashboard has received. The most popular dashboards are refreshed every hour, the less popular dashboards are refreshed every 24 hours. Popular dashboards are refreshed via the community cluster.

**Here is an overview of the different execution triggers:**

*   interactive dashboard execution
    
*   interactive query execution
    
*   scheduled query execution
    
*   scheduled dashboard execution
    
*   API query execution
    
*   popular dashboard executions
    

[​](https://docs.dune.com/query-engine/query-executions#query-engine-size)

Query engine size
-----------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Dune has three query engine sizes: **small**, **medium**, and **large**. The query engine size determines the amount of resources allocated to your query. The larger the query engine, the more resources are allocated to your query. This means that queries executed on a larger query engine will run faster and are less likely to time out.

#### 

[​](https://docs.dune.com/query-engine/query-executions#small-engine-size)

Small engine size

The Free engine is the default query engine for all queries on Dune. It is a shared cluster, meaning that it is used by all Dune users. This means that the community cluster can be busy at times if many users are running queries at the same time. To avoid long loading times and timeouts, we recommend using the medium or large engine for resource-intensive queries.  
Executions on the free engine are free of charge and will time out after 2 minutes.

#### 

[​](https://docs.dune.com/query-engine/query-executions#medium-engine-size)

Medium engine size

Run queries manually or programmatically. Credits consumed based on actual compute resources used. Suitable for most standard queries and dashboards.

#### 

[​](https://docs.dune.com/query-engine/query-executions#large-engine-size)

Large engine size

Run queries with maximum timeout and resources. Credits consumed based on actual compute resources used. Ideal for complex queries and heavy workloads.

Was this page helpful?

# Teams on Dune - Dune Docs

[Skip to main content](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/teams#content-area)

[Dune Docs home page![light logo](https://mintcdn.com/dune/uyJ-jHeSRFvNrzyu/logo/dune-logo-light.png?fit=max&auto=format&n=uyJ-jHeSRFvNrzyu&q=85&s=fbdf0e7e6fabc31e49afcdb53cb5e774)![dark logo](https://mintcdn.com/dune/uyJ-jHeSRFvNrzyu/logo/dune-logo-dark.png?fit=max&auto=format&n=uyJ-jHeSRFvNrzyu&q=85&s=767370d661596e21a7b3a4525d50d77e)](https://dune.com/)

Search...

⌘K

Search...

Navigation

Analytics Studio

Teams on Dune

[Get Started](https://docs.dune.com/home)
[Analytics Studio](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/overview)
[Query Engine](https://docs.dune.com/query-engine/overview)
[Data Catalog](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/overview)

On this page

*   [Why Teams?](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/teams#why-teams%3F)
    
*   [Creating a Team](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/teams#creating-a-team)

[​](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/teams#why-teams%3F)

Why Teams?
-------------------------------------------------------------------

Creating a Team has several benefits:

1.  **Collaborate on the same content.** Teams make it easy for multiple Wizards to work on shared Queries and Dashboards.
2.  **Shared access to paid features.** All Team members can spend credits and access paid features like private Queries and Dashboards.
3.  **A new Team profile.** Showcase all of your Team’s work in one place.
4.  **User roles.** Onboard Team members as viewers, editors or admins.

### 

[​](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/teams#creating-a-team)

Creating a Team

Head over to [**Settings > Teams**](https://dune.com/settings/teams)
 to create your Team.

### 

[​](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/teams#adding-users)

Adding users

You can invite other Dune Wizards to join your Team in the People section of your Team’s Settings page. When you invite someone you’ll need to input their Dune Username. You’ll also need to assign them one of the following **Roles**:

*   👀 **Viewer:** can see the Team’s content through My Creations and will be listed as a Team member in the Team page. Can also spend credits.
*   ✏️ **Editor:** in addition to the above, they can create and edit Queries under the Team’s domain.
*   ⚙️ **Admin:** in addition to the above, they can manage the Team and its content.

When you invite a Wizard to join your team we’ll email them a link to join. They can also directly go to [Settings > Teams](https://dune.com/settings/teams)
 and accept their invite there.

### 

[​](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/teams#team-content)

Team content

Team Queries and Dashboards are created the same way they are for individual accounts. The context you are in determines whether you are creating content for your personal account or for your Team. You can always change the ownership of a Query or Dashboard in their Settings page. ![Team content](https://mintcdn.com/dune/aF4zRBqDzf2PxRoY/web-app/images/teams/teams-1.png?w=2500&fit=max&auto=format&n=aF4zRBqDzf2PxRoY&q=85&s=328959f82aefc45320dc4743d6217975)

Once you transfer content to a Team, you will only be able to transfer it out of the Team if you are an Admin. If you accidentally transfer content to a Team you will have to ask the Team’s Admin to transfer it back to you.

[​](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/teams#switching-contexts)

Switching Contexts
---------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Once you are member of a team, you can switch between your personal context and your Team context. Accordingly, the “my creations” page will show your personal creations or your team’s creations.  
Additionally, all queries and dashboards created in the team context will be owned by the team and not by you personally. ![](https://mintcdn.com/dune/kuKkfe7NiZRF86tb/web-app/images/context-switcher.jpeg?w=2500&fit=max&auto=format&n=kuKkfe7NiZRF86tb&q=85&s=71074320cb3fd224042a80611aeb03ae) The context predicates which credit balance you are spending from. If you are in your personal context, you will spend your personal credits. If you are in your Team’s context, you will spend your Team’s credits.  
You can spend the credits of your team on any content, regardless of whether it is owned by your personal account, your team or another Wizard. You can edit the content of your team, regardless of whether you are in the personal or team context. In the [Version History](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/query-editor/version-history)
 edits you make will be attributed to your personal account, even if you are in your Team’s context.

### 

[​](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/teams#faq)

FAQ

Can I have private content?

Private dashboards and queries are available for the team or personal account they are in.

How do I edit my role?

You have to ask one of your team admins. If you’re an admin, you will still have to ask another admin or upgrade someone else to the admin role. That’s to ensure every team always has at least an admin.

Can I remove people from my Team?

Yes, you can remove people from your Team in the People section of your Team’s Settings page.

Can I transfer content to another Team?

Yes, you can transfer content to another Team in the Settings page of the Query or Dashboard you want to transfer.

Can I transfer content to another Wizard?

Yes, you can transfer content to another Wizard in the Settings page of the Query or Dashboard you want to transfer. This will only work if the other Wizard is a member of your Team. If they are not, you will have to invite them to your Team first.

Can I transfer content to my personal account?

Yes, you can transfer content to your personal account in the Settings page of the Query or Dashboard you want to transfer.

**I have feedback, how do I reach out?** Come join our [#general-feedback Discord channel](https://discord.com/channels/757637422384283659/1012706316755664926)
 and we’ll be glad to help 🙇‍♂️

# Create Graphs - Dune Docs

[Skip to main content](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/visualizations/charts-graphs#content-area)

[Dune Docs home page![light logo](https://mintcdn.com/dune/uyJ-jHeSRFvNrzyu/logo/dune-logo-light.png?fit=max&auto=format&n=uyJ-jHeSRFvNrzyu&q=85&s=fbdf0e7e6fabc31e49afcdb53cb5e774)![dark logo](https://mintcdn.com/dune/uyJ-jHeSRFvNrzyu/logo/dune-logo-dark.png?fit=max&auto=format&n=uyJ-jHeSRFvNrzyu&q=85&s=767370d661596e21a7b3a4525d50d77e)](https://dune.com/)

Create Visualizations

Create Graphs

[Get Started](https://docs.dune.com/home)
[Analytics Studio](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/overview)
[Query Engine](https://docs.dune.com/query-engine/overview)
[Data Catalog](https://docs.dune.com/data-catalog/overview)
[Analytics API](https://docs.dune.com/api-reference/overview/introduction)
[Datashare](https://docs.dune.com/datashare/datashare)
[Catalyst](https://docs.dune.com/catalyst/overview)

On this page

*   [Visualization Configuration Options](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/visualizations/charts-graphs#visualization-configuration-options)
    
*   [X/Y-axis Tick and Label formats](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/visualizations/charts-graphs#x%2Fy-axis-tick-and-label-formats)
    

**Visualizations make your data come to life! You can create Visualizations from any results of a query.**

On Dune you can create a variety of different graphs and charts to visualize your data.

Bar Charts

![bar chart example](https://mintcdn.com/dune/kuKkfe7NiZRF86tb/web-app/images/charts-graphs/bar-chart-example.png?w=2500&fit=max&auto=format&n=kuKkfe7NiZRF86tb&q=85&s=f209ee6996a68b1bdc71af6478f11f66)

Area Charts

![area chart example](https://mintcdn.com/dune/kuKkfe7NiZRF86tb/web-app/images/charts-graphs/area-chart.png?w=2500&fit=max&auto=format&n=kuKkfe7NiZRF86tb&q=85&s=4786100cba4f970b4eb6e1671d0e6371)

Scatter Charts

![scatter chart example](https://mintcdn.com/dune/kuKkfe7NiZRF86tb/web-app/images/charts-graphs/scatter-chart-example.png?w=2500&fit=max&auto=format&n=kuKkfe7NiZRF86tb&q=85&s=0d82ad0597560b3fceab58488a5debed)

Line Charts

![line chart example](https://mintcdn.com/dune/kuKkfe7NiZRF86tb/web-app/images/charts-graphs/line-chart-example.png?w=2500&fit=max&auto=format&n=kuKkfe7NiZRF86tb&q=85&s=bcfc6e28e1dc0143e02f5922d02cc490)

Pie Charts

![pie chart example](https://mintcdn.com/dune/kuKkfe7NiZRF86tb/web-app/images/charts-graphs/pie-chart-example.png?w=2500&fit=max&auto=format&n=kuKkfe7NiZRF86tb&q=85&s=04dcb76783d87935521583d923f58702)

Mixed Graphs

![mixed graph example](https://mintcdn.com/dune/kuKkfe7NiZRF86tb/web-app/images/charts-graphs/mixed-graph-example.png?w=2500&fit=max&auto=format&n=kuKkfe7NiZRF86tb&q=85&s=a2c4ff95a67d66268d0cd677d08c0c85)

You can mix all of these graph types in one Visualization, as long as your base graph isn’t a Pie chart. All graph Visualizations share a common set of editing options, see the tabs below for how to configure each. ![all visualization configuration options](https://mintcdn.com/dune/kuKkfe7NiZRF86tb/web-app/images/charts-graphs/all-visualization-configuration-options.png?w=2500&fit=max&auto=format&n=kuKkfe7NiZRF86tb&q=85&s=2a6dd2b6a60ce366ffbf635c8c033f8b)

[​](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/visualizations/charts-graphs#visualization-configuration-options)

Visualization Configuration Options
------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------------

*   Chart options
    
*   Result data
    
*   X-axis options
    
*   Y-axis options
    
*   Series options
    
*   Pie options
    

This section allows you to define how to display your data.![see explanations below](https://mintcdn.com/dune/kuKkfe7NiZRF86tb/web-app/images/charts-graphs/graphs-4.png?w=2500&fit=max&auto=format&n=kuKkfe7NiZRF86tb&q=85&s=eeaf2da596b6bbb8a6380aab6bb1f877)**Title**

*   The title will appear in all instances of this graph prominently at the top.
*   The graph will always keep the name of the Query, even if you edit this.

**Show chart legend**

*   Ticking this box will enable or disable the legend for the chart.

**Enable stacking**

*   If applicable, ticking this box will stack the chart values on top of each other based on the x-axis values.
*   If this is not turned on, the values will be plotted individually on the y-axis.
*   The calculation underpinning this will always group the value corresponding to one value on the x-axis. Make sure your data is clean in able for this to work (avoid gaps in your data).

**Normalize to percentage data**

*   This will normalize the chart to display percentage values of the chosen data table.
*   The calculation underpinning this will always group the value corresponding to one value on the x-axis. Make sure your data is clean in able for this to work (avoid gaps in your data).

**Show data labels**

*   Ticking this box leads to the display of the individual datapoints inside of the graph.
*   This only makes sense in cases where you have few datapoints that are spread out far enough from each other to not overlap.

### 

[​](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/visualizations/charts-graphs#x%2Fy-axis-tick-and-label-formats)

X/Y-axis Tick and Label formats

![image](https://mintcdn.com/dune/kuKkfe7NiZRF86tb/web-app/images/charts-graphs/graphs-8.png?w=2500&fit=max&auto=format&n=kuKkfe7NiZRF86tb&q=85&s=43c573aa100324be68c21de4e34a61fc) Tick formats change how numeric values and axis labels in your graphs are displayed. Here’s how to format them:

| Starting Value | Tick/Label format | Output | Description |
| --- | --- | --- | --- |
| 1256784.3745 | `[blank]` | 1256784.3745000 | Displays the number 7 decimal precision. |
| 1256784.3745 | `0` | 1256784 | Displays only the integer. |
| 1256784.3745 | `0,0` | 1,256,784 | Only displays the integer with comma separation. |
| 1256784.3745 | `0,0.00` | 1,256,784.38 | Displays the number with `[x]` decimal precision, where `[x]` is the number of `0` you add after the decimal point. |
| 1256784.3745 | `0.0a` | 1.2M | Displays the number with `[x]` precision and a letter based on the number’s `1e[y]` power (eg “m” for million, “b” for billion) |
| 1256784.3745 | `$0.0a` | $1.2M | Adds a ”$” to the number. Works with all formats above though use of the `a` suffix is recommended. Currently the only ”$” is the only supported currency symbol. |

[​](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/visualizations/counters#counters)

Counters
-------------------------------------------------------------------------------

Counters are a great way to provide your audience with immediate “on a glance” stats. !["on a glance" stats in https://dune.com/0xBoxer/NFT](https://mintlify.s3.us-west-1.amazonaws.com/dune/web-app/visualizations/web-app/images/other-visualizations/counters-1.png)

### 

[​](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/visualizations/counters#configuring-your-counter)

Configuring your Counter

![Counters 2](https://mintcdn.com/dune/6vWXO_JiAjw4C8nz/web-app/images/other-visualizations/counters-2.png?w=2500&fit=max&auto=format&n=6vWXO_JiAjw4C8nz&q=85&s=7f26a944893cdbaba857bf09f928020f)

#### 

[​](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/visualizations/counters#counter-options)

Counter options

In this section you can define what kind of data the counter should display:

Display Title

*   The Title will appear in all instances of this graph prominently at the top.
*   If left blank, the Query name will be the only thing that is left standing.

Column Selection

*   In this field, you can define which column the counter should show.

Row Selection

*   This field can be used to define which row of the underlying data table you want displayed, e.g., row 1.
*   Usually, this requires you to sort or limit your Query results in order for row 1 to show the wanted results.

#### 

[​](https://docs.dune.com/web-app/visualizations/counters#formatting)

Formatting

This section is where you can adjust how your numerical data is displayed.

Prefix Setting

*   This field allows you to define a prefix for your counter value.
*   e.g.: `$`, `€`, `Ξ`, `฿`

Suffix Setting

*   This field allows you to define a suffix for your counter value.

Label Setting

*   This field allows you to define a label for your counter value.
*   The label will appear beneath the counter value as text.

Decimal Setting

*   In this field, you can choose how many decimals you want displayed for your counter.

![label](https://mintcdn.com/dune/6vWXO_JiAjw4C8nz/web-app/images/other-visualizations/counters-label-1.png?w=2500&fit=max&auto=format&n=6vWXO_JiAjw4C8nz&q=85&s=12e480cf7fc145cb6f133c12a63bf886)
